Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Nullification by Removal of Excuse
Ruling on nullifiers of prayer and intra-Hanafi dispute on basis of nullification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nullification of prayer when an excuse for tayammum is removed, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between al-Barda'i and al-Karkhi, including the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Prayer is nullified by removal of excuse, but the reason is not that exiting prayer is fard—it is that the fard itself changes.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah presents a list of events that nullify prayer, then delves into a critical intra-Hanafi dispute about why removal of an excuse (e.g., recovery from illness) nullifies prayer before the final sitting. Two Imams, Abu Sa'id al-Barda'i and Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, offered conflicting analyses of Abu Hanifa's ruling. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between the ruling itself and its underlying logical basis—a key skill for advanced fiqh analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its examples
Read the list of nullifiers given by the author: removal of tayammum excuse, end of wiping period, removing khuff, illiterate learning a verse, naked finding covering, one gesturing gaining ability to bow. All nullify prayer if they occur before sitting for tashahhud.
The common condition: the event happens before the final sitting (qa'dah).
2
State the textual evidence
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud is cited: 'When you say this, or do this, your prayer is complete.' The completion is attached to the sitting, so no further conditions can be added. This is a naqli (textual) proof.
The hadith supports that the prayer is complete with the sitting; extra conditions would be an addition.
3
Analyze al-Barda'i's argument
Al-Barda'i argued that since prayer is only nullified by leaving a fard, and the only thing remaining is exiting prayer, exiting must be fard. He deduced this from the nullification cases.
His position is based on qiyas (analogy): nullification only occurs by omitting a fard.
4
Analyze al-Karkhi's rebuttal
Al-Karkhi countered that exiting prayer is not fard; if it were, it would be specific to salām, which is an act of worship. Instead, these events change the nature of the fard itself (e.g., the obligation to use water after tayammum). The nullification is because the fard is altered, not because exiting is omitted.
The reliance is on the text: the hadith attaches completion to sitting, not to any act of exiting.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The later authorities (al-Mujtaba, al-Mi'raj, al-Ta'sis) preferred al-Karkhi's view. The relied-upon position is that exiting by one's own action is not fard, and nullification occurs because the fard changes.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if exiting were fard, additional conditions could be imposed; now they cannot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذه أيضاً وكذا تبطل بزوال كل عذر أباح التيمم (و) كذلك (تمام مدة ماسح الخف) وتقدم بيانها (و) كذا نزعه) أي الخف، ولو بعمل يسير لوجوده قبل القعود قدر التشهد (وتعلم الأمي آية) ولم يكن مقتدياً بقارىء نسبة إلى أمة العرب الخالية عن العلم والكتابة كأنه كما وسواء تعلمها بالتلقي أو تذكرها ووجدان العاري ساتراً) يلزمه الصلاة فيه فخرج نجس الكل وما لم يبحه مالكه وقدرة الموحي على الركوع والسجود) لقوة باقيها فلا يبني ولدته أمه والأركان بدليل ما في حديث ابن مسعود إذا قلت هذا، أو فعلت هذا فقد تمت صلاتك حيث علق التمام بالقعدة فمن شرط شيئاً آخر فقد زاد على النص، وهي نسخ، ولم يجز بالرأي واختلف في الوجه للإمام فذهب أبو سعيد البردعي إلى أنه إنما قال بالبطلان لأن الخروج من الصلاة بصنع المصلي فرض عنده لأنها لا تبطل إلا بترك فرض، ولم يبق عليه سوى الخروج بصنعه، فلولا أنه فرض لما فسدت بتركه وتبعه على ذلك العامة كما في العناية، وذهب أبو الحسن الكرخي إلى أن البطلان عنده باعتبار ان هذه المعاني مغيرة للفرض كنية الإقامة فاستوى في حدوثها أول الصلاة وآخرها ولا خلاف بينهم في أن الخروج بصنعه ليس بفرض، وإنما استنبطه البردعي من هذه المسائل، وهو غلط منه لأنه لو كان فرضاً كما زعمه لاختص بما هو قربة، وهو السلام قال في المجتبى : والمحققون من أصحابنا على قول الكرخي، وفي المعراج معزياً للحلواني، والصحيح ما قاله الكرخي ، قال صاحب التأسيس: ما قاله أبو الحسن أحسن اهـ.
This also: similarly, it is nullified by removal of every excuse that permitted tayammum, and likewise completion of the period of wiping over the khuff (its explanation preceded), and likewise removal of the khuff, even with a small action, if it occurs before sitting for the amount of the tashahhud. And the illiterate person learning a verse while not following a reader (attribution to the Arab nation devoid of knowledge and writing, as if he was like...). And it is the same whether he learned it by receiving or remembered it. And the naked person finding a covering that necessitates prayer in it, so excluded is clothing that is entirely impure or that its owner does not permit. And the one making gestures gaining ability to bow and prostrate due to the strength of the remainder, so he does not build [upon the previous prayer]. And the pillars, as evidence by what is in the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'When you say this, or do this, your prayer is complete' where completion is attached to the sitting, so whoever stipulates something else has added to the text, and it is abrogation, and it is not permissible by opinion. And there is disagreement on the aspect regarding Imam [Abu Hanifa]. Abu Sa'id al-Barda'i held that he only ruled nullification because exiting prayer by the action of the worshipper is fard in his view, since prayer is only nullified by leaving a fard, and nothing remains upon him except exiting by his action; if it were not fard, it would not be corrupted by leaving it. The general body followed him, as in al-'Inayah. Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi held that nullification in his view is due to these meanings changing the fard, like the intention of the iqamah, so they are equal in occurring at the beginning or end of prayer. There is no disagreement among them that exiting by his action is not fard; al-Barda'i merely deduced it from these issues, and it is an error from him because if it were fard as he claimed, it would be specific to what is an act of worship, which is the salām. It is stated in al-Mujtabā: 'The verifiers among our companions are on the statement of al-Karkhi.' In al-Mi'raj, attributed to al-Hilwani: 'The correct is what al-Karkhi said.' The author of al-Ta'sis said: 'What Abu al-Hasan said is better.' End.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah presents a ruling on factors that nullify prayer, followed by an intra-Hanafi dispute about the logical basis of nullification. The ruling states that prayer is nullified by: removal of an excuse that permitted tayammum (e.g., recovery from illness or safety from danger before sitting for tashahhud), completion of the period for wiping the khuff (1 day for resident, 3 days for traveler), removal of the khuff even with a small action, an illiterate person learning a verse while not following a reciter, a naked person finding a covering, and one gesturing gaining ability to bow and prostrate. The commentary then delves into a key dispute: why does removal of the excuse nullify the prayer? Abu Sa'id al-Barda'i argued that exiting prayer by one's own action is fard (obligatory), so leaving it nullifies. Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi countered that these occurrences change the fard (the obligation) itself, similar to changing intention, and that exiting by one's own action is not fard. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of al-Karkhi, as confirmed by al-Mujtaba and other authorities. This distinction is crucial: it affects whether additional conditions can be imposed on the text of the hadith.

Key Terms
الخروج بصنعه (al-khurūj bi-ṣun‘ihī): The act of exiting prayer by one's own deliberate action, such as saying salām or performing an act that terminates prayer.
الفرض (al-farḍ): An obligatory element of prayer whose omission invalidates the prayer entirely.
القعدة (al-qa‘dah): The sitting posture at the end of prayer after the final prostration, specifically for reciting the tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, why does removal of an excuse for tayammum nullify the prayer if it occurs before the final sitting?
A) Because exiting prayer by one's own action is a fard and omitting it nullifies.
B) Because the removal changes the fard (obligation), making the previous prayer invalid.
C) Because the person must renew his intention.
D) Because the prayer time becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the nullification of prayer by removal of an excuse is not because exiting is fard but because the fard itself changes, as per al-Karkhi's preferred view.

Ruling on Illiterate Person Learning a Verse While Following a Reciter
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nullification for an illiterate following a reciter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling and the mufta bihi position on whether an illiterate person's prayer is nullified when he learns a verse while following a reciter.

Core Idea
Following a reciter prevents nullification when an illiterate learns a verse — the corrected view in al-Ẓahīriyyah.

This passage addresses a nuanced issue: an illiterate person who cannot recite the Fatihah suddenly learns a verse during prayer. Does this nullify the prayer? The answer depends on whether he is following a reciter. The general body held nullification, but the later fatwa collection al-Ẓahīriyyah corrected this view, and it was adopted by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling context
The act is an illiterate person (al-ummī) learning a verse while in prayer. The ruling is whether the prayer becomes nullified (bāṭil).
The illiterate person is defined as one who cannot recite the Fatihah.
2
Locate the ikhtilaf
The general body ('āmmah) holds that learning a verse nullifies the prayer. However, the text from al-Ẓahīriyyah corrects this: it is not nullified when the person is following a reciter.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.
3
Understand the condition of following a reciter
The key condition is that the illiterate person must be following a reciter (muqtadī bi qāri') at the time of learning. If he is not following, the original ruling of nullification applies.
The mufta bihi position adopts this exception.
4
Recognize the authority weight
The original ruling is from the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, but the exception is from al-Ẓahīriyyah, a later fatwa collection. The adoption by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi gives it weight in practice.
This reflects the Hanafi tendency to prefer later fatwa collections for practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولم يكن مقتدياً بقارىء) اختلف فيما لو كان الأمي خلف قارىء أي وقد تعلم آية، والعامة على البطلان لكن صحح في الظهيرية عدمه. قال الفقيه أبو الليث : وبه نأخذ قوله : (كأنه كما ولدته أمه هذا لا يناسب سابقه، وإنما يناسب لو كان منسوباً إلى أمه، فيقال في بيان وجه النسبة كأنه الخ فتدبر . قوله : (وسواء تعلمها بالتلقي أو تذكرها) قد علمت أن هذا مفروض فيما إذا حصل أحد هذه الأشياء قبل القعود قدر التشهد أما لو كان بعده، فإن التعلم بالتلقي لا يفسدها اتفاقاً لأنه عمل كثير . قوله : (يلزمه الصلاة فيه بأن كان مالكاً له، أو أبيح له وهو طاهر، أو نجس، وعنده ما يطهره به أو لا إلا أن ربعه طاهر. قوله : (وقدرة المومي على الركوع والسجود لقوة باقيها هذا يفيد أن القدرة حصلت بعد ركوع، وسجود بالإيماء فأما إذا حصلت قبل فعلهما ، أصلاً، فلا بناء لضعيف على قوي في ذلك فلا تفسد
His statement: 'and he was not following a reciter' — there is disagreement regarding if the illiterate person was behind a reciter, i.e., and he had learned a verse; the general body holds nullification, but it is considered correct in al-Ẓahīriyyah that it is not nullified. Al-Faqīh Abu al-Layth said: 'We adopt this.' His statement: 'as if he were as his mother bore him' — this does not fit the preceding, but rather fits if he was attributed to his mother, so it is said in explaining the aspect of attribution: 'as if he...' so reflect. His statement: 'and it is the same whether he learned it by receiving or remembered it' — you have known that this is presumed when one of these things occurs before sitting for the amount of tashahhud. As for if it was after, then learning by receiving does not nullify by agreement because it is a great action. His statement: 'the prayer becomes obligatory for him in it' — meaning he is the owner, or it is permitted to him, and it is pure, or impure, and he has something to purify it with, or not, except that a quarter of it is pure. His statement: 'and the one gesturing gaining ability to bow and prostrate due to the strength of the remainder' — this indicates that ability occurred after bowing and prostrating by gesture. As for if it occurred before them at all, then there is no building from weak upon strong in this matter, so it is not nullified.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage examines several sub-rulings related to the nullification of prayer. First, if an illiterate person (who cannot recite) is following a reciter and then learns a verse, the general opinion says prayer is nullified, but the correct view in al-Ẓahīriyyah is that it is not nullified. The commentator, al-Tahtawi, explains the phrase 'as if he were as his mother bore him' – this analogy actually fits if the person is attributed to his mother (i.e., a bastard), not the previous context. Then, he clarifies that whether the illiterate person learns the verse by direct teaching or by remembering, the ruling applies only if it occurs before sitting for tashahhud. If it occurs after that, learning by direct teaching does not nullify because it is considered a great amount of action (kathīr). Next, the naked person who finds a covering must wear it for the prayer, provided he owns it or has permission, and it is pure or can be purified (unless only a quarter of it is pure). Finally, for one performing prayer by gesture, if he gains ability to bow and prostrate after having already gestured, the prayer is not nullified because the strong does not build upon the weak. But if he gains ability before performing the gestures at all, then the prayer is nullified, and he must restart.

Key Terms
الأمي (al-ummī): A person who cannot read or recite Qur'an; in this context, one who cannot recite the Fatihah.
الظهيرية (al-Ẓahīriyyah): A reference to a work or position, likely al-Ẓahīriyyah by al-Ẓahīrī or similar, where the correct view is recorded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the corrected view (mufta bihi), when does an illiterate person's prayer NOT nullify despite learning a verse?
A) When he learns it by himself.
B) When he is following a reciter.
C) When he learns it after sitting.
D) When he learns it during prostration.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that an illiterate person's prayer is not nullified if he learns a verse while following a reciter.

Timing of Learning and Effect on Prayer Nullification
Refinement of timing condition and gesturing scenario

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate the ruling on an illiterate person learning a verse before vs after sitting for tashahhud, and explain why gaining ability to bow/prostrate after gesturing does not invalidate prayer.

Core Idea
Before sitting: learning nullifies; after sitting: it does not, because it is a great action.

This passage continues from the previous ruling, clarifying the timing condition. Whether the illiterate person learns by direct teaching or by remembering, the key factor is when it occurs. The commentator also addresses a related scenario: a person praying by gesture who then gains ability to bow and prostrate. The ruling depends on whether ability occurs before or after performing the gesture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two timings
The passage distinguishes between learning before sitting for tashahhud and after sitting. Before sitting is the subject of the ikhtilaf; after sitting is agreed upon.
The amount of sitting is the time needed for tashahhud.
2
Understand the reason for the difference
Learning after sitting is considered a great action (kathīr), which does not nullify the prayer by agreement. This is because extensive movement (in this case, learning/reciting) is overlooked after the prayer is essentially complete.
The concept of kathīr vs qalīl is key.
3
Apply the rule to the gesturing scenario
If a person is praying by gesture due to inability to bow/prostrate, and then he gains the ability after having already gestured, the prayer is not nullified – the strong (actual ability) does not build upon the weak (gesture).
If ability is gained before any gesture, the prayer is nullified and must be repeated.
4
Contrast the two cases
The principle is that once an action is performed in a valid manner (even if incomplete), later improvement does not invalidate it. Similarly, learning after the prayer is nearly complete does not invalidate it.
This is consistent with the Hanafi principle of not building strong upon weak.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولم يكن مقتدياً بقارىء) اختلف فيما لو كان الأمي خلف قارىء أي وقد تعلم آية، والعامة على البطلان لكن صحح في الظهيرية عدمه. قال الفقيه أبو الليث : وبه نأخذ قوله : (كأنه كما ولدته أمه هذا لا يناسب سابقه، وإنما يناسب لو كان منسوباً إلى أمه، فيقال في بيان وجه النسبة كأنه الخ فتدبر . قوله : (وسواء تعلمها بالتلقي أو تذكرها) قد علمت أن هذا مفروض فيما إذا حصل أحد هذه الأشياء قبل القعود قدر التشهد أما لو كان بعده، فإن التعلم بالتلقي لا يفسدها اتفاقاً لأنه عمل كثير . قوله : (يلزمه الصلاة فيه بأن كان مالكاً له، أو أبيح له وهو طاهر، أو نجس، وعنده ما يطهره به أو لا إلا أن ربعه طاهر. قوله : (وقدرة المومي على الركوع والسجود لقوة باقيها هذا يفيد أن القدرة حصلت بعد ركوع، وسجود بالإيماء فأما إذا حصلت قبل فعلهما ، أصلاً، فلا بناء لضعيف على قوي في ذلك فلا تفسد

Validity of Present Prayer When Remembering a Missed Prayer
Hashiya commentary on ruling for remembering a fā'itah while in salāh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a present prayer remains valid when a missed prayer is remembered during it, and apply the Hanafi principle of tartib to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
Present prayer valid if missed prayer made up before fifth prayer ends — the missed prayer count becomes six.

This lesson examines a critical refinement in Hanafi fiqh: what happens when you remember a missed obligatory prayer while already engaged in a present one. The matn states the prayer is valid under specific conditions, and the hashya clarifies the role of forgetfulness and the expansive nature of the time for qada'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the event
We have a present prayer (e.g., 'Asr) being performed, and during it the person remembers a missed obligatory prayer (e.g., Zuhr).
The person must be bound by tartib (obligation to maintain order).
2
Determine the ruling from the matn
The matn states the present prayer is valid (sahih) and its invalidity is lifted, but this is conditional.
The ruling is not absolute; it depends on the person's situation.
3
Identify the first condition: tartib and spacious time
The person must be 'bound by order' (li dhi tartib) and the time for the present prayer must be 'spacious' (s'a), meaning there is enough time to complete the present prayer and also make up the missed one before the current prayer's time ends.
If time is constrained, the present prayer may be invalid.
4
Understand the hashya's refinement: forgetfulness
The hashya clarifies that the condition 'remembering' is important. If the person had forgotten the missed prayer, the obligation of tartib is lifted, and the present prayer is valid regardless.
The ruling only applies to one who remembers during the prayer.
5
Identify the second condition: making up the missed prayer
The text adds that the present prayer becomes valid 'because the missed prayers become six by including the one first left out'. This implies the missed prayer must be made up before the time of the fifth prayer (i.e., the next prayer after the one being performed) ends.
The number six references the five daily prayers plus one missed, making six that must be performed in order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتذكر فائتة لذي ترتيب عليه، أو على إمامه ولو وترا في الوقت سعة . قوله : (متذكراً الفائتة) إنما قيد به لأنه لو كان ناسياً يسقط الترتيب به فيعتبر حينئذ تذكر فيه لا ما نسي فيه. قوله: (صحت وارتفع فسادها لصيرورة الفوائت ستاً بضميمة المتروكة أولاً.
His statement: 'And he remembers a missed prayer for one bound by order (tartib), whether it is obligatory upon him or upon his imam, even if it is witr, in the expansive time.' His statement: 'Remembering the missed prayer' – he restricts it because if he had forgotten, the order is waived, so the consideration is remembrance at that moment, not what he forgot. His statement: 'It is valid and its invalidity is lifted, because the missed prayers become six by including the one first left out.'
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This is a critical commentary (hashiya) on the matn of Maraqi al-Falah, discussing what happens when a person remembers a missed obligatory prayer while performing a present prayer. The matn states that if the person is bound by the order of qada' (tartib, maintaining sequence between missed and present prayers) and remembers the missed prayer during the present prayer, the ruling depends on whether the time for the present prayer is spacious. The commentator clarifies that the restriction to 'remembering' means that if he had forgotten the missed prayer, the obligation of sequence is lifted, and the present prayer is valid. He then explains that if he remembers, performs the present prayer, and then makes up the missed prayer before the time of the fifth prayer ends, the present prayer is valid and its invalidity is removed because the missed prayers become six (including the one he first omitted).

Key Terms
فائتة (fā'itah): A missed obligatory prayer (fard or wajib) that must be made up (qada').
لذي ترتيب (li dhi tartīb): One who is obligated to maintain the chronological order of prayers, i.e., performing present prayer only after making up missed ones.
صحت وارتفع فسادها (ṣaḥḥat wa irtafa'a fasādahā): The present prayer is valid and its invalidity is lifted, meaning it is considered correct and not requiring repetition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when does a present prayer become valid despite remembering a missed prayer during it?
A) If the missed prayer is made up before the time of the fifth prayer ends.
B) If the missed prayer is made up immediately after the present prayer.
C) If the present prayer is performed in congregation.
D) If the person forgot the missed prayer during the present prayer.

Key Takeaway
A present prayer performed while remembering a missed prayer is valid only if the missed prayer is made up before the end of the fifth prayer's time.

Appointing an Unfit Imam: Timing and Validity
Hashiya on a matn ruling about invalidators of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ruling on appointing an unfit imam in prayer, identify the exception based on timing after the qa'dah, and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Appointing an unfit imam invalidates prayer unless after the first sitting.

This lesson examines a ruling from Maraqi al-Falah on what invalidates prayer. The hashya by al-Tahtawi clarifies that while appointing an unfit imam normally spoils the prayer, there is a critical timing exception: if the appointment occurs after the qa'dah of the first sitting (qadr al-tashahhud), the prayer is considered complete and valid according to the chosen view. We will unpack the legal reasoning and the intra-Hanafi difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The act is 'istikhlaf' – appointing a replacement imam during prayer. The default ruling in the matn is that appointing someone unfit (e.g., an illiterate or excused person) invalidates the prayer.
The matn lists this among invalidators of prayer.
2
Locate the exception
The hashya adds that if the appointment happens after the qa'dah (first sitting) of the prayer, the prayer is not invalidated but considered valid.
This exception applies only when the appointment occurs after performing the tashahhud in the first sitting.
3
Understand the basis for the exception
The action of appointing an imam after the qa'dah is not considered excessive (amal kathir) because the prayer is nearly complete, and there is no necessity to appoint an unfit person.
This is based on the principle that actions after the qa'dah do not break the prayer as long as they are not frequent.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Ja'far and Fakhr al-Islam hold that the prayer is complete (tammah) by consensus after the qa'dah. The standard Zahir al-Riwayah position is that it invalidates, but the later authorities (al-Fath, Sahib al-Kafi) adopt the exception as mufta bihi.
This refinement shows the development of fatwa within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستخلاف من لا يصلح إماماً) كأمي ومعذور (وطلوع الشمس في الفجر ) لطر والناقص على الكامل (وزوالها) أي الشمس (في) صلاة (العبد)ين ودخول وقت العصر في الجمعة لفوات شرط صحتها وهو الوقت وسقوط الجبيرة عن برء) لظهور الحدث السابق وزوال عذر (المعذور) بناقض ويعلم زواله
And the appointment of one who is not fit to be an imam, like an illiterate (ammi) or excused person, and sunrise during Fajr for the appearance of deficiency over perfection, and its zenith, i.e., the sun, in the prayer of the two Eids, and the entry of Asr time in Jumu'ah due to the loss of a condition of its validity which is time, and the falling of a cast after healing due to the appearance of the previous event (hadath) and the removal of the excuse of the excused person by something that nullifies wudu, and the removal is known by a complete time passing without it.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage from the hashiya lists several things that spoil prayer, including the appointment of an unfit imam. The matn states that if an unfit person (like one who cannot recite proper Quran or one with a valid excuse) is appointed as imam during the prayer, this invalidates the prayer. However, the commentary (not fully shown here) adds that if this appointment occurs after the qa'dah of the first sitting (qadr al-tashahhud), then according to Abu Ja'far and Fakhr al-Islam, the prayer is considered complete (tammah) by consensus. This is because the act of appointing an imam after that point is not considered a frequent action (amal kathir) that invalidates the prayer, as there is no necessity to appoint an unfit imam. The other matn phrases (sunrise, zenith, etc.) are separate rulings that will be addressed in other lessons.

Key Terms
استخلاف (istikhāf): Appointing a replacement imam during prayer after the original imam becomes unable to continue.
أمي (ummī): An illiterate person who cannot recite Quran properly, thus unfit to lead prayer.
معذور (ma'dhūr): A person with a valid excuse, e.g., incontinence of urine, who cannot avoid impure discharge, thus their imamate is invalid for normal people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) When the appointment occurs after the qa'dah of the first sitting (qadr al-tashahhud).
C) When the unfit imam is also ma'dhūr.
D) When the appointment is made during the recitation.

Key Takeaway
The appointment of an unfit imam invalidates prayer by default, but if it occurs after the first sitting (qa'dah), the prayer remains valid according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Temporal Events That Invalidate Prayer: Sunrise, Zenith, Asr Entry, and Cast Removal
Hashiya listing specific temporal events that invalidate ongoing prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four temporal events that invalidate an ongoing prayer according to the Hanafi school, state the rule for each, and explain the condition about occurring before the tashahhud.

Core Idea
Prayer is invalidated by sunrise during Fajr, zenith during Eid, entry of Asr during Jumu'ah, and falling of a cast—each subject to precise timing and conditions.

This lesson from the Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies when an ongoing prayer becomes invalid due to external temporal events. The text discusses four scenarios: sunrise during Fajr prayer, the sun reaching zenith during the two Eid prayers, the entry of Asr time during Jumu'ah prayer, and the falling of a medical cast without healing. Understanding these exceptions helps ensure the validity of one's prayers, as defaults may change under specific circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Event
List the four events: sunrise, zenith, entry of Asr time, and falling of a cast. Note the specific prayer context for each.
Each event is linked to a particular prayer: Fajr for sunrise, Eid for zenith, Jumu'ah for Asr entry, and any prayer for cast falling.
2
Determine Invalidity Condition
For each event, check if it occurs before the qa'dah of tashahhud. Invalidity applies only if the event occurs before this sitting. If after, the prayer is generally valid.
The passage states: 'before the tashahhud' (قبل التشهد). After qa'dah there is disagreement among mashayikh.
3
Apply Intra-Hanafi Differences
For the entry of Asr time during Jumu'ah, note the difference between Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn. According to Abu Hanifa, invalidity occurs when the shadow becomes double (second mithl); according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, when the first mithl begins.
This difference is explicitly mentioned. The text does not give a tarjih, so both views are operative in different contexts.
4
Handle Exceptional Cases
The falling of a cast invalidates only if it falls due to healing. If it falls without healing (e.g., accidentally), the prayer remains valid. For a mustahadah, if her bleeding stops during prayer before tashahhud, her prayer becomes invalid if she performed wudu on the assumption of continued excuse.
These nuances prevent blanket application of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وطلوع الشمس في الفجر) ليس المراد أن ينظر إلى القرص، بل إذا رأى الشعاع الذي لو لم يكن ثمة جبل يمنعه لرأى القرص كما في التبيين، وكذا إذا دخل وقت الثلاثة على مصل للقضاء قوله : الطر والناقص) وهو وقت طلوعها لأنه وقت عبادة عابديها قوله : (على الكامل وهو ما قبل الطلوع لعدم حصول ذلك النقص فيه قوله : (وزوالها أي الشمس في صلاة العيدين لفوات شرطها، وهو وقت الضحى كذا في الشرح والذي في الشرح العيد بالإفراد وفيما رأيته من نسخ الصغير أن العيد بالمداد الأحمر، والياء والنون، علامة التثنية بالمداد الأسود. قوله : ( ودخول وقت العصر في الجمعة) قد علمت أن موضوع المسائل فيما قبل التشهد فإذا دخل أول المثل الثاني على قولهما أو انقضى المثل على قوله : فسدت على قولهما في الأول، وفي الثاني على قوله لا الأول، وأما إذا كان بعد القعود قدر التشهد ففيه الخلاف بين المشايخ، وبحث فيه بأنه كيف يتحقق الخلاف بينهم مع اختلافهم في دخول وقت العصر، وأجيب بأنه يمكن أن يطيل الجلوس بعدما قعد قدر التشهد إلى أن يصير الظل مثليه، وتمامه في شرح السيد، وإنما قيد بالجمعة لأن الظهر لا يبطل بدخول وقت العصر، وما في مجمع الأنهر عن السراجية قيل : تخصيص الجمعة إتفاقي لأن الحكم في الظهر كذلك اهـ غريب قوله : (عن) (بره) قيد به لأنها لو سقطت لا عن برء لا تفسد قوله : ( بناقض ) متعلق بقوله : المعذور وصورته توضأت مستحاضة مع السيلان، وشرعت في الظهر فقبل القعود قدر التشهد انقطع الدم ودام الانقطاع ، إلى غروب الشمس، وكذا لو توضأت على الانقطاع فوجد قبل الشروع في الصلاة، أو بعده، وأما لو توضأت وصلت على الإنقطاع فلا تلزمها الإعادة مطلقاً تبين زوال عذرها أم لا اهـ من السيد ملخصاً.
His statement: 'And sunrise during Fajr' – the meaning is not to look at the disc, but when he sees the rays such that if there were no mountain preventing it, he would see the disc, as in al-Tabyin. Likewise, when the time of the third [prayer] enters upon one praying qada'. His statement: 'the deficient and the perfect' – which is the time of its rising because it is the worship time of its worshippers. His statement: 'upon the perfect' – which is before sunrise because that deficiency does not occur in it. His statement: 'And its zenith, i.e., the sun, in the prayer of the two Eids' – due to the loss of its condition, which is the time of Duha, as in the sharh. And in the sharh it is 'Eid' in the singular, and in what I have seen of copies of al-Saghir, 'Eid' is in red ink, and the ya and nun marking the dual are in black ink. His statement: 'And the entry of Asr time in Jumu'ah' – you have known that the subject of the issues is before the tashahhud. So if the beginning of the second mithl enters according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), or the mithl passes according to him (Abu Hanifa), it [the prayer] becomes invalid according to the two in the first, and according to him [Abu Hanifa] in the second, not the first. And if it is after the qa'dah of the tashahhud, then there is disagreement among the mashayikh. And it is discussed: how can there be disagreement among them given their difference over the entry of Asr time? The answer: he can prolong the sitting after he has performed the qa'dah of the tashahhud until the shadow becomes double. Its completion is in Sharh al-Sayyid. It is restricted to Jumu'ah because Zuhr is not invalidated by the entry of Asr time. And it is said in Majma' al-Anhar from al-Sirajiyyah: the specification of Jumu'ah is agreed upon because the ruling for Zuhr is likewise. This is strange. His statement: 'by healing' – he restricts it because if it falls without healing, it does not invalidate. His statement: 'by something that nullifies wudu' – it is related to his statement 'the excused person'. Its scenario: a woman with istihadah performed wudu while blood was flowing, and started Zuhr prayer; then before qa'dah of tashahhud, the blood stopped, and the stoppage continued until sunset. Similarly, if she performed wudu on the stoppage and then blood appeared before starting prayer or after. But if she performed wudu and prayed on the stoppage, she does not have to repeat at all, whether her excuse ended or not. End of summary from al-Sayyid.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage from the hashiya discusses several times and events that can invalidate an ongoing prayer. The commentator clarifies each one: (1) Sunrise during Fajr prayer: The prayer becomes invalid when the sun begins to rise, not by seeing the disc but by the appearance of the rays that would reveal the disc if not obstructed. (2) The terms 'the deficient and the perfect' relate to the time of sunrise; after sunrise is the worship time of sun worshippers, considered deficient. Before sunrise is the perfect time for Fajr. (3) Zenith of the sun during the two Eid prayers: The Eid prayer loses its condition (time of Duha) if the sun reaches zenith, as its prescribed time is Duha (forenoon). (4) Entry of Asr time during Jumu'ah: According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, if the shadow reaches the first mithl (equal to the object's height after noon), the Jumu'ah prayer becomes invalid. According to Abu Hanifa, it becomes invalid only when the shadow becomes double (second mithl). These details apply before the qa'dah of tashahhud; after that, there is disagreement. The restriction to Jumu'ah is because Zuhr prayer is not invalidated by the entry of Asr time. (5) Falling of a cast after healing: If the cast falls off due to healing and the previous hadath (like minor impurity) appears, the prayer is invalidated because the excuse (cast) is removed. But if it falls before healing, the prayer remains valid. The case of a mustahadah (woman with chronic bleeding) is given as an example: if her blood stops during prayer before qa'dah and remains stopped, her prayer becomes invalid because her excuse is lifted. If she performed wudu before the stoppage and then the stoppage occurred, she repeats if it stopped before or during prayer, but if she prayed continuously on the stoppage, she does not repeat.

Key Terms
المثل (al-mithl): A unit of shadow measurement: the length of an object's shadow after noon. The first mithl is when the shadow equals the object's height; the second mithl is when it is double.
استحاضة (istihāḍah): Chronic uterine bleeding not related to menstruation or childbirth; a condition that excuses a woman from some purity requirements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when does the Jumu'ah prayer become invalid due to the entry of Asr time according to Abu Hanifa?
A) When the shadow becomes equal to the object's height (first mithl).
B) When the shadow becomes double the object's height (second mithl).
C) When the muezzin calls for Asr prayer.
D) When the sun passes the zenith.

Key Takeaway
The conditions for invalidation of prayer by temporal events are precise: they apply only before the tashahhud and are subject to specific definitions and intra-Hanafi differences.

Nullifiers of Prayer: Hadath, Unconsciousness, and Muhadhat
Listing of nullifiers with detailed conditions and intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five categories of events that nullify prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the conditions under which building (bina) is permitted after a hadath.

Core Idea
Prayer is nullified by intentional hadath, unconsciousness, madness, janabah, and alignment with a desirable woman; only heavenly hadath allows building.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi enumerates the events that invalidate an ongoing prayer. It provides critical refinements on the conditions for building after a hadath and the precise requirements for nullification through muhadhat. Understanding these nullifiers is essential for the worshipper to know when a prayer must be repeated and when it can be salvaged through building.

Guided Path
1
List the nullifiers
Identify the five categories: intentional hadath, hadath caused by someone else, unconsciousness/madness, janabah (from looking or wet dream), and muhadhat (alignment with a desirable woman).
2
Examine building conditions
Distinguish between intentional hadath and hadath by another (no building allowed) and heavenly hadath (unintentional, allows building with renewal of wudu).
Heavenly hadath includes events beyond human control, like a stone drawing blood.
3
Analyze janabah nuances
Janabah by looking or wet dream invalidates prayer. For wet dream, the sleep must not itself have invalidated the prayer; if the man is mu-tamakkin (firmly seated) and sleeps without invalidating, the wet dream causes nullification.
4
Dissect muhadhat rulings
Understand the conditions: the woman must be desirable (fit for intercourse), the alignment must occur during prayer with shared tahrimah, and the limb specified is the shank and heel. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad requires alignment during a complete rukn; Abu Yusuf holds that any amount invalidates.
The mufta bihi is Muhammad's view as chosen in al-Fath.
5
Apply generality
The ruling applies to all prayers except funeral prayer (which has no sujud). It also applies only when both individuals are in the same prayer (either both following an imam or one following the other).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الأصح) كذا في التبيين. قال في النهر ولا دليل عليه، والتفسير الصحيح لها ما في المجتبى، وهو أن تقوم المرأة بجنب الرجل، أو قدامه من غير حائل وفي الدر المعتبر المحاذاة بعضو واحد، وخصه الزيلعي بالساق And intentional hadath – meaning he does not precede it, because with it he builds [prayer with building] (أو بصنع غيره) like a stone falling that draws blood. And unconsciousness, madness, and janabah attained by looking or wet dream of a sleeping person who is mu-tamakkin, and alignment of a desirable woman by her shank and heel in the more correct view, even if she is a mahram to him or a wife he desires, even if she is past youth like an ugly old woman, in the performance of a rukn according to Muhammad or its amount according to Abu Yusuf. His statement: (أو بصنع غيره) i.e., hadath caused by another; it is invalidating because building is not allowed, since the condition for permissible building is that it be heavenly. His statement: (ومحاذاة المشتهاة) i.e., alignment of a man with a desirable woman. Restriction by 'desirable' excludes alignment with an amrad (beardless youth) which does not invalidate; some have invalidated it but have no support in the transmitted reports. The invalidation in the case of a woman is not caused by the arousal of desire, but rather the fard of the place is abandoned, as in al-Fath. It is general, including free woman, slave, ajnabiyyah, wife, and ugly old woman. A desirable woman is one fit for intercourse, and age is not considered as corrected by the sharh. In al-Durr: a desirable woman currently, like a nine-year-old absolutely, or eight or seven if large, or past youth like an old woman. End. His statement: (by her shank and heel in the more correct view) – this is in al-Tabyin. In al-Nahr it is said there is no evidence for it, and the correct interpretation is what is in al-Mujtaba: that the woman stands beside the man or in front of him without a barrier. In al-Durr, alignment is considered by one limb, and al-Zaylai specifies it as shank and heel. In al-Khaniyyah: if the woman prays in that manner and the man is lower than her beside her or behind her, if any limb of the man aligns with a limb of her, his prayer becomes invalid due to the existence of alignment with part of her body. But here there is no alignment with shank and heel. His statement: (in the performance of a rukn according to Muhammad) – it was chosen in al-Fath and confirmed by al-Halabi like the author. In al-Khaniyyah, both little and much alignment invalidates, and this is attributed to Abu Yusuf. His statement: (في صلاة) – it is general, including if she intended Zuhr behind one praying Asr, then it is a transfer (naql) according to the madhhab.

Commentary
This is a comprehensive passage from the hashiya enumerating actions and events that nullify (invalidate) an ongoing prayer. The commentator explains each item of the matn: (1) Intentional hadath (ritual impurity): If a person deliberately breaks his wudu, the prayer becomes invalid. The commentary clarifies that if hadath occurs unintentionally (without his action), he can 'build' (bina: continue the prayer after renewing wudu). This is because intentional hadath does not allow building. (2) Hadath caused by someone else (e.g., a stone falls on him and causes bleeding): This also invalidates because the hadath is not heavenly (samawi), and building is only allowed for heavenly hadath. (3) Unconsciousness and madness: Even if brief, they invalidate prayer. (4) Janabah attained by looking (e.g., if he looks and becomes aroused to the point of ejaculation during prayer) or by a wet dream while asleep, provided the sleep does not itself invalidate the prayer; the wet dream causes janabah which invalidates. (5) Alignment (muhadhat) of a man with a woman who is desirable: This invalidates the man's prayer if her shank and heel are aligned during performance of a rukn (according to Muhammad) or its amount (according to Abu Yusuf). The qualification 'desirable' excludes beardless boys and old women who are not desirable. The commentator gives details: the restriction to 'man' indicates he must be mukallaf; a boy's prayer is not invalidated. The alignment must occur during the prayer when both are in prayer. The correct view distinguishes the case of a mahram or wife. The definition of 'desirable' includes young girls and old women, but the condition of actual desirability is not age-dependent. The interpreter details that alignment by a single limb suffices, and the limb specified as shank and heel is the most correct view. There is also a dispute between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf: Muhammad says invalidity occurs only if alignment lasts during a rukn; Abu Yusuf says even a small amount (qadr) invalidates. Some sources consider any alignment invalidating. (6) The phrase 'في صلاة' makes the ruling general for all prayers including funeral prayer? No, it says 'مطلقة' so it does not invalidate funeral prayer because it has no sujud. Also, 'مشتركة تحريمة' means the invalidity applies when both are sharing the same tahrimah (i.e., they are in a joint prayer, either both following an imam or in an imam-follower relationship). The commentary also discusses the case of a woman intending Zuhr behind a man praying Asr – this is considered a transfer (naql) of intent, which is invalid.

Key Terms
محاذاة المشتهاة (muḥādhāt al-mushtahāt): A man and woman praying in such a way that their bodies are aligned horizontally (side by side or one in front of the other without a barrier), which invalidates the man's prayer if the woman is desirable and both are in the same prayer.
حدث سماوي (ḥadath samāwī): A hadath that occurs without human action, like urine incontinence or wind due to illness; considered 'heavenly' and allows building upon renewal of wudu.
بنيان (binyān): Continuing a prayer after a hadath by renewing wudu and then resuming from where one stopped, without starting the prayer over.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the condition for a woman to be considered 'desirable' (mushtahah) for the ruling of muhadhat?
A) She must be a young virgin.
B) She must be fit for intercourse, regardless of age.
C) She must be a non-mahram.
D) She must be praying the same prayer as the man.

Key Takeaway
The nullification of prayer by muhadhat is not based on desire but on the existence of alignment with a woman fit for intercourse, and building after hadath is only permitted for heavenly hadath.

Conditions for Muhadhah Invalidating Prayer
Explains the conditions under which a woman's alignment invalidates prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nine conditions for muhadhah to invalidate the prayer and apply the ruling to scenarios involving commonality in performance and the imam's intention.

Core Idea
Muhadhah invalidates only if nine specific conditions are met – including the imam's intention to lead her.

The issue of a woman's alignment with a man in prayer (muhadhah) is nuanced in the Hanafi school. Contrary to a common assumption, not every alignment breaks the prayer. Building on the previous lesson's foundation, this passage from al-Tahtawi's hashya clarifies the exact conditions that must be present for muhadhah to render the prayer invalid. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying the ruling in congregational prayer settings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
What is the default: does alignment invalidate the man's or woman's prayer? The text says her prayer becomes invalid, not his, if the man signals and she doesn't step back.
The man's prayer remains valid unless he is the imam and fails to signal.
2
List the nine conditions
The passage enumerates conditions: woman desirable, alignment with calf/heel, during a rukn, absolute prayer, common tahrimah, unified place, no barrier, no signal, imam's intention. Write them down.
These conditions must all be present for invalidation.
3
Analyze the condition of commonality
Understand the two types: commonality in tahrimah (opening takbir) and commonality in performance (ada'). Both are required.
If they are not performing the same action simultaneously, no invalidation.
4
Examine the proof for signaling
The text cites the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (mawquf) as evidence that the imam must signal the woman to step back. Reflect on how this hadith indicates the obligation.
The hadith is interpreted as an explanation of the Quranic 'degree'.
5
Assess the debate on imam's intention
The majority require the imam's intention to lead her for alignment to invalidate. However, there is a narration that allows iqtida' without intention if no alignment initially.
The mufta bihi is that intention is a condition.

الفراغ الذي يكون بين القدمين ومحل السجود أي موضع منه، أو لا بد من كونها بين قدميها وقدميه وعليه إنما يكون إذا تحاذت الأقدام فأما لو تقدم عليها هل يعتبر كونها بحذاء قدميه، أو قدميها، وهذه حادثة الفتوى في الفتح، وقد يستدل بحديث إمامته لأنس واليتيم حيث قامت العجوز من وراء أنس واليتيم، فقد قامت منفردة خلف الصف، وهو مفسد عند الإمام أحمد، ومكروه عندنا فلولا أن المحاذاة مفسدة ما أخرها لإرتكاب المكروه اه فلو لم يشر إليها لتتأخر بعد ما دخلت في الصلاة فقد ترك فرض المقام فتفسد صلاته دون صلاتها إلا إذا كان المحاذي الإمام، وأطلق في الإشارة فشمل ما إذا كانت من المؤتم وهو المتبادر . قوله : وتاسع شروط المحاذاة الخ) وأولها المشتهاة ثانيها أن يكون بالساق، والكعب على ما ذكره ثالثها أن تكون في أداء ركن أو قدره رابعها أن تكون في صلاة مطلقة. خامسها أن تكون في صلاة مشتركة تحريمة سادسها إتحاد المكان سابعها عدم الحائل ثامنها عدم الإشارة إليها بالتأخر . قوله : (أن يكون الإمام قد نوى (إمامتها) هذا القيد مستغنى عنه لعلمه من قيد الاشتراك إذ لا اشتراك إلا بنية الإمام إمامتها لأنه إذا لم ينو إمامتها لا يصح إقتداؤها بحر ولا فرق في ذلك بين صلاة وصلاة وهو قول الجمهور كما في الكافي والتبيين وإنما لا يصح إقتداؤهن بدون نية إمامتهن إذا وجدت المحاذاة أما إذا لم تحاذ أحداً ففي رواية صح إقتداؤها بلا نية الإمام لها لأنه لا فساد في الحال واحتماله في المآل بأن تمشي خطوة، أو خطوتين فتحاذي الرجل أمر موهوم والظاهر أن لا تفعله لكراهتاه فإن فعلت وحاذت بطل إقتداؤها لفوات شرطه، وهو نية الإمام، ولم تبطل صلاة من حاذته لعدم صحة إقتدائها، وفي رواية لا يصح اقتداؤها لأنه لما احتمل الفساد من جهتها توقف ذلك على اختيارها بلا اعتبار الأحوال كذا في الكافي، والتبيين وغاية البيان والحاصل أن محاذاتها لا توجب فساد صلاة أحد بدون نية الإمام إمامتها في جميع الصلوات
In a unified place, even if legally, by her standing on something less than a man's height without a barrier the size of a cubit or a gap that can accommodate a person, and he did not signal to her to step back. If she does not step back at his signal, her prayer becomes invalid, not his. He is not obliged to [mention] the tahrimah, i.e., from the perspective of tahrimah. Its meaning is what the author mentioned. Some added the restriction of performance, meaning that they must have an imam in what they perform, actually like those who catch up, or estimatively like those who are late. These are two conditions in the commonality. As for tahrimah, it is by agreement; as for performance, it is the correct view as in al-Idah from Sharh al-Talkhis. So much so that if hadath preceded them and she aligned with him while they were going for wudu, or when coming before engaging in the action of prayer, there is no invalidation due to lack of commonality in performance at the time of alignment because this state is not a state of performance. Similarly, if they were ma'sbuq and she aligned with him after the imam's salam in what they are making up, there is no invalidation because the ma'sbuq is alone in what he makes up, even though commonality in tahrimah exists in both cases. It is not a condition of commonality in tahrimah that she catch the beginning of the imam's prayer according to the correct view. Rather, if he preceded her by a rak'ah or more and she aligned with him in what she caught, his prayer becomes invalid as in al-Bahr from al-Siraj. If it is said: Mentioning commonality in performance suffices from mentioning commonality in tahrimah, and for that, it was sufficed with in Talkhis al-Jami'. The answer is that they mentioned each one separately to detail the place of disagreement from the place of agreement. Thus in al-Idah. His saying: (In a unified place): If the place differed, such as the woman being in a high place such that nothing of her aligns with anything of him, it does not invalidate. His saying: (Even if legally, by her standing...) This from him follows the correct view that it is not required that it be with the calf and foot, which contradicts what he chose earlier, so consider. His saying: (The size of a cubit): i.e., in thickness of a finger. It was estimated with it because it is the least state of sitting, and it is close to this amount, so it was estimated with it. Consider whether it suffices for her to be placed in the space between the two feet and the place of prostration, i.e., any place of it, or must she be between his feet and her feet? According to this, it is only when the feet align. But if she advances, is it considered alignment with his feet or her feet? This is an incident for fatwa, so it should be referred. Perhaps they took this estimation from the sutra, for the Lawgiver considered this amount a barrier between the praying person and the passer-by, even preventing sin. His saying: (Or a gap) is conjunctive to barrier. This estimation is from al-Zayla'i and those after him followed him. His saying: (And he did not signal to her to step back): He is commanded to make her step back due to what is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud as a mawquf: 'Keep them back from where Allah kept them back.' Even though it is ahad, it indicates obligation because it occurred as an explanation of the mujmal of the Book, which is His saying: 'And for men is a degree over them' [al-Baqarah: 2]. He said in al-Fath: And it may be cited by the hadith of his imamah of Anas and the orphan when the old woman stood behind Anas and the orphan, so she stood alone behind the row. This is invalidating according to Imam Ahmad, and makruh according to us. If alignment were not invalidating, she would not have been made to step back to avoid makruh. So if he did not signal to her to step back after she entered prayer, he has left a fard of standing, so his prayer invalidates, not hers, unless the one aligning is the imam. He made the signal absolute, so it includes when it is from the muqtadi, which is apparent. His saying: (And the ninth of the conditions of the invalidating alignment): The first: that she be desirable; second: that it be with the calf and heel as he mentioned; third: that it be during performance of a rukn or its equivalent; fourth: that it be in an absolute prayer; fifth: that it be in a prayer common in tahrimah; sixth: unity of place; seventh: absence of a barrier; eighth: absence of signaling to her to step back. His saying: (That the imam has intended to lead her): This condition is dispensed with because it is known from the condition of commonality, since there is no commonality except with the imam's intention to lead her. Because if he does not intend to lead her, her iqtida' is not valid, and there is no difference in that between one prayer and another, and it is the saying of the majority as in al-Kafi and al-Tabyin. Indeed, her iqtida' is not valid without his intention to lead her only when alignment occurs. But if she does not align with anyone, in one narration her iqtida' is valid without the imam's intention for her, because there is no invalidation in the present, and the possibility in the future, such as her taking a step or two and aligning with a man, is a speculative matter, and it is apparent that she will not do it due to its karahah. If she does and aligns, her iqtida' becomes invalid due to the loss of its condition, which is the imam's intention, and the prayer of the one she aligned with does not invalidate due to the unsoundness of her iqtida'. In another narration, her iqtida' is not valid because when the possibility of invalidation is from her side, it depends on her choice without consideration of states, as in al-Kafi, al-Tabyin, and Ghayat al-Bayan. The conclusion is that her alignment does not cause invalidation of anyone's prayer without the imam's intention to lead her in all prayers.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from al-Tahtawi's hashya, discussing the conditions under which a woman's alignment (muhadhah) with a man in prayer invalidates the prayer. It begins by stating the basic ruling: if a woman aligns with a man in a single place (or legally unified), without a barrier, within a cubit's distance, and he does not signal her to step back, then her prayer is invalidated but not his. The text then expands on the concept of 'commonality' (ishtirak) in prayer, distinguishing between commonality in tahrimah (the opening takbir) and commonality in performance (ada'). Both are required for invalidation. Several scenarios are discussed: if hadath preceded them while they were going for wudu, no invalidation because commonality in performance is absent; similarly for ma'sbuq (latecomers) making up prayers. The correct view is that in tahrimah, it is not necessary to catch the beginning of the imam's prayer. The passage then details the estimation of the cubit, taken from the sutra (screen) used to prevent passers-by. The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud ('Keep them back...') is cited as proof for the obligation to have women stand behind, indicating that alignment is invalidating. Finally, the nine conditions for invalidating alignment are enumerated: the woman must be desirable (mushthahan), alignment must be with the calf and heel, during performance of a rukn or its equivalent, in an absolute prayer, in a prayer common in tahrimah, in a unified place, no barrier, no signal to step back, and the imam must have intended to lead her. The last condition is debated; the majority hold that without intention, the alignment does not invalidate the man's prayer. The commentary is dense and assumes knowledge of Hanafi fiqh principles.

Key Terms
المحاذاة (al-muhadhah): The alignment of a woman praying in the same row as a man, which under certain conditions invalidates the prayer.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The commonality in the opening takbir of the prayer, i.e., both entered the state of ihram together.
الإشتراك في الأداء (al-ishtirak fi al-ada'): Commonality in performance, meaning they are executing the same part of the prayer simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The woman must be desirable (mushthahan)
B) The imam must have intended to lead her
C) The alignment must occur in the same row
D) There must be a barrier between them

Key Takeaway
Muhadhah invalidates the woman's prayer only when all nine conditions are present, including the imam's intention to lead her and absence of a barrier.

Hadath During Prayer: Permissible and Invalidating Actions
Explains rulings when hadath precedes during prayer and its effect on reading and motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a prayer remains valid after hadath and identify which actions invalidate it.

Core Idea
Hadath does not automatically invalidate prayer; only Quranic recitation and unnecessary walking do, but tasbih is allowed.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi delves into the precise Hanafi ruling on a person who experiences hadath (invalidating wudu) during prayer. It clarifies that not all speech or movement after hadath breaks the prayer; specific exceptions like tasbih, tahil, and istighfar are permitted. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for any practitioner who wishes to correctly handle such a situation and avoid invalidating the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the occurrence of hadath
Recognize that hadath during prayer triggers a specific set of rulings regarding subsequent actions.
2
Distinguish permissible and impermissible actions
Understand that reciting Quran and unnecessary walking invalidate the prayer, while tasbih, tahil, and istighfar do not.
These dhikr phrases are not considered part of the prayer's integral recitation.
3
Understand the layf wa nashr structure
The text uses a dispersed and arranged structure: 'for wudu' connects to 'going', and 'completing prayer' connects to 'returning'.
This clarifies that the permission to walk is only for the necessary journey to purify and return.
4
Role of intention
The intention during the motion matters: if one intends purification, the prayer can be built upon; if no intention, the prayer is invalidated.
There is a difference of narration on this point; the relied-upon position requires intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله من سبقه الحدث سواء كان رجلاً أو امرأة. قوله : (ولو اضطر إليه) وفي الخانية إذا اضطر إلى الكشف يبني وإلا لا وبه جزم في التنوير، وشرحه. قوله : (لا تسبيح) مثله التهليل والاستغفار فإنها لا تفسد بها لأنه ليس من أجزائها كما البحر فالمراد بالتسبيح الذكر غير القرآن قوله لف ونشر أي مرتب فقوله : للوضوء مرتبط بقوله : ذاهباً ، وقوله : إتمام الصلاة مرتبط بقوله، أو عائداً . قوله : ذاهباً، وعائداً) لف ونشر مرتب كذا أفاده في الشرح، وفيه أنه في الذهاب اجتمع الحدث والمشي، وهذا إنما يظهر إذا سبقه الحدث حال القيام أما إذا كان بعد الركوع، أو السجود، فلا إلا إذا قلنا أنه يشبه أداء الركن وعبارتهم مطلقة. قوله : ( بنية التطهير إلخ) وتفسد إذا لم ينو شيئاً على إحدى الروايتين كما في الدر ولو رفع قائلاً سمع الله لمن حمده لا یبنی لأن الرفع محتاج إليه للإنصراف
His saying: 'Who hadath preceded him' whether man or woman. His saying: 'And even if he is forced to it'? In al-Khaniyya, if he is forced to uncover, he builds; otherwise no, and it is affirmed in al-Tanwir and its commentary. His saying: 'Not tasbih' similarly tahil and istighfar, for they do not invalidate because they are not from its parts, as in al-Bahr. So what is meant by tasbih is dhikr other than the Quran. His saying: 'Layf wa nashr' i.e., arranged. So his saying: 'for wudu' is connected to his saying: 'going', and his saying: 'completing the prayer' is connected to his saying: 'or returning'. His saying: 'going and returning' is arranged layf wa nashr, as indicated in the sharh. And in it, that in going, the hadath and walking combine. This only appears if hadath preceded him while standing; but if after ruku or sujud, then no, unless we say it resembles performing a rukn, and their expression is absolute. His saying: 'With intention of purification etc.' And it invalidates if he intended nothing according to one of the two narrations, as in al-Durr. And if he raised saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', he does not build because the raising is needed for the departure.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement discussing the ruling on a person who experiences hadath (ritual impurity) during prayer and its effect on subsequent actions. It begins by noting that the ruling applies equally to men and women. If one is forced to uncover (e.g., to perform wudu), they may build upon their prayer according to al-Khaniyya; otherwise not. The text then distinguishes between reciting the Quran (which invalidates) and tasbih, tahil, istighfar (which do not invalidate) because they are not part of the prayer. The author explains a 'layf wa nashr' (dispersed and arranged) structure: the phrase 'for wudu' relates to 'going', and 'completing the prayer' relates to 'returning'. The combination of hadath and walking occurs when hadath occurs during standing; if it occurs after ruku or sujud, it does not combine unless considered akin to performing a rukn. Finally, the intention during the motion matters: if one intends purification, it is valid; if no intention, the prayer invalidates. Raising the head for 'Sami'a Allah' does not count as building because it is needed for departure.

Key Terms
سبق الحدث (sabaq al-hadath): The occurrence of ritual impurity (invalidating wudu) during prayer before completing it.
التسبيح (al-tasbih): Uttering phrases like 'Subhanallah' as dhikr, which does not invalidate the prayer if done after hadath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a person, after experiencing hadath during prayer, recites tasbih (Subhanallah)?
A) The prayer is invalidated because it is speech
B) The prayer is not invalidated because tasbih is not from the integral parts of prayer
C) The prayer becomes makruh but remains valid
D) The person must immediately leave the prayer

Key Takeaway
Tasbih, tahil, and istighfar are permissible after hadath in prayer; reciting Quran is not.

Ninth Condition of Invalidating Alignment: Imam's Intention
Explains the ninth condition for invalidating alignment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ninth condition for invalidating alignment in congregational prayer and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the imam's intention to lead women.

Core Idea
Alignment alone does not invalidate prayer unless the imam intended to lead the women.

In the Hanafi school, the invalidating alignment (al-muhadhat al-mufsida) of a woman beside men in prayer is not automatically corrupting. One of its key conditions is that the imam must have intended to lead her. This lesson unpacks this ninth condition, showing how the requirement of intention is implicit in the general principle of sharing (ishtirak) between imam and follower, and explores an internal Hanafi difference on whether a woman's following can be valid without such intention when alignment is initially absent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act under discussion is a woman aligning with men in congregational prayer. The ruling is that this alignment is invalidating (mufsida) only if a set of conditions are met. The ninth condition is that the imam had the intention to lead the woman (niyat imamatha).
This is a condition for the alignment to be legally harmful, not a standalone ruling.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites mainstream Hanafi sources (al-Kafi, al-Tabyin) and states that this is the view of the majority (qawl al-jumhur). The underlying proof is the principle that valid following (iqtida') requires the imam's intention, as sharing (ishtirak) in prayer cannot occur without it.
The dalil is not a direct Quranic or hadith text but a widely accepted usul principle.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The link between the principle and the condition: Since iqtida' depends on the imam's intention, when a woman aligns herself with the imam, her following is only valid if the imam had intended to lead her. Without his intention, she is not in his prayer, and therefore the alignment does not affect the validity of anyone's prayer.
The condition is implicit in the very definition of 'following' (iqtida').
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Two narrations are mentioned: (1) If no initial alignment occurred, a woman's following is valid even without the imam's intention, because the risk of future alignment is too speculative. (2) The second narration requires intention always, because even the possibility of future corruption suffices. The text indicates reliance on the first narration.
This difference affects practical cases where a woman joins a congregation without the imam explicitly intending to lead her.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and mufta bihi
The mufta bihi is the first narration: alignment without intention does not invalidate. This is supported by the reasoning that a woman is unlikely to move and cause alignment (due to its dislike). The text explicitly states that her alignment does not cause invalidity of anyone's prayer without the imam's intention.
The reliance is on al-Kafi and al-Tabyin, indicating preference for the permissive narration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Book of Prayer. (And) the ninth of the conditions of the invalidating alignment is that the imam has intended to lead her. If he did not intend it, she is not in his prayer, so the alignment is negated. He said: 'That the imam has intended to lead her' — this condition is dispensed with because it is known from the condition of sharing, since there is no sharing except by the imam's intention to lead her, because if he did not intend to lead her, her following him is not valid, whether it be a man or a woman, and there is no difference in this between one prayer and another, and it is the statement of the majority, as in al-Kafi and al-Tabyin. Indeed, their following is not valid without his intention to lead them when alignment exists. But if she did not align anyone, in one narration her following is valid without the imam's intention for her because there is no corruption in the present and its possibility in the future — that she takes one or two steps and aligns a man — is something imagined, and it is apparent that she will not do it due to its dislike. If she does and aligns, her following becomes invalid due to the loss of its condition, which is the imam's intention, but the prayer of the one she aligns does not become invalid because her following is not valid. In another narration, her following is not valid because when corruption is possible from her side, it depends on her choice without considering circumstances, as in al-Kafi, al-Tabyin and Ghayat al-Bayan. The conclusion is that her alignment does not cause the invalidity of anyone's prayer without the imam's intention to lead her in all prayers.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi discusses the ninth condition for the invalidating alignment (muhadhat mufsida) in congregational prayer: the imam must have intended to lead the women. The author notes that this condition is implicit in the general condition of sharing (ishtirak) between imam and follower, as there is no valid following without the imam's intention. The ruling applies equally to men and women. The passage presents two narrations regarding the validity of a woman's following when she aligns after the fact: one deems it valid if no alignment occurred initially, the other invalid because of potential future corruption. The relied-upon position is that alignment only invalidates if the imam intended to lead.

Key Terms
المحاذاة المفسدة (al-muhadhat al-mufsida): The alignment of a woman alongside male worshippers in prayer, which can invalidate the prayer of those she aligns under certain conditions.
نية الإمامة (niyat al-imamah): The imam's intention to lead specific followers/women in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence if a woman aligns with the imam without the imam having intended to lead her?
A) Her prayer becomes invalid immediately.
B) The imam's prayer becomes invalid.
C) The alignment does not invalidate due to the missing condition.
D) She must repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
For alignment to be invalidating, the imam must have intended to lead the woman; otherwise, alignment does not affect validity.

Invalidation by Passing Nearby Water
Ruling with conditions on water proximity invalidation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which passing a nearby water source invalidates prayer and identify when building (bina') is permitted.

Core Idea
Passing water more than two rows intentionally without excuse invalidates prayer.

This lesson covers a specific invalidation of prayer related to water. It explains the distance threshold, the requirement of intention and excuse, and the ruling on building after returning from fetching water. Understanding these conditions helps avoid unintended nullification of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is passing a nearby water source during prayer. The ruling: it invalidates prayer (mufsid) under specific conditions.
Ruling from al-Bahr and other sources.
2
Determine the conditions for invalidation
Invalidation requires: distance more than two rows, intentional (without excuse), and availability of a tool (e.g., bucket string).
If distance is two rows or less, or with excuse, prayer remains valid.
3
Recognize the building (bina') issue
After returning from fetching water, the person may build (continue prayer) but must repeat the bowing or prostration that occurred before leaving, according to the more cautious view.
Intra-Hanafi difference: Muhammad requires repeating the pillar; Abu Yusuf requires repeating the standing/sitting.
4
Analyze the exceptions
Exceptions: if the place is narrow, or the person forgot, or needed to draw water from a well, then passing does not invalidate.
Tayammum is like wudu in a place where water is present.

His statement: (sunan of purification) like wiping the whole head, rinsing mouth and nose three times according to the most correct, as in the sharh, and the first is to say 'and doing the sunan'. His statement: (and it is the desert) — the pronoun refers to 'other than it'. His statement: (even if there is no row in front of him) — with fatha on hamza of 'amam. Know that if he prays in the desert and thinks that he had hadath, so he goes from his place, then learns that he did not have hadath: if he is praying in a congregation, then the place of the rows has the ruling of the mosque, so that if he reaches the last of the rows without exceeding them, he builds; if he exceeds them, he does not. Even if he goes forward, the limit is the sutra; if he exceeds it, his prayer invalidates. If there is no sutra in front of him, then the amount of rows behind him, such that if he goes forward an amount that if he had gone back he would have exceeded the rows…
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi covers several additional invalidators of prayer. First, passing a nearby water source by more than two rows intentionally without excuse invalidates, but if the distance is equal to two rows or less, it does not. Excuses like narrow space or forgetting prevent invalidation. Second, leaving the mosque due to suspecting hadath without excuse invalidates, but leaving for a legitimate purpose like correction (islah) does not by istihsan. Third, exceeding the rows (sufuf) or sutra in the desert (non-mosque) invalidates; but if there is no sutra, a person is excused as long as they stay within the area of their prostration place. The passage also discusses details about building (bina') after hadath according to Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and various conditional rulings regarding purification, water, and rows.

Key Terms
السترة (al-sutra): An object placed in front of the praying person to demarcate the space for prayer in open areas.
الصفوف (al-sufuf): The rows of worshippers in congregational prayer; in the desert, the extent of the rows determines the area protected from invalidation.
ماء قريب (ma' qarib): A water source that is near enough to the praying person to be considered within the prayer area.
خرز دلو (kharz dalw): A bucket string used to draw water from a well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Any distance if intentional

Key Takeaway
Passing nearby water invalidates only if intentional, without excuse, and by more than two rows; building after returning requires repeating affected parts.

Conditions for Building After an Unintentional Hadath
Commentary on building conditions and invalidators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which building after an unintentional hadath is permissible and identify the intra-Hanafi difference regarding rare external causes.

Core Idea
Building is allowed only for a preceding heavenly hadath; rare events are not included.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on continuing prayer after an unintentional hadath. The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi outlines the conditions for valid building and distinguishes between permissible and impermissible movements, as well as the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognise that 'building' (bina') refers to continuing salah from where you left off after purification, not restarting. The ruling is permissible (mubah) under specific conditions.
This is a concession, not an obligation.
2
Distinguish 'preceding' from 'overcoming'
A 'preceding hadath' occurs without one's intent and is beyond control (heavenly). 'Overcoming' happens when one is aware but cannot control it. Only the first allows building.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh.
3
Identify conditions for valid building
The hadath must be unintentional, the movement for purification must be for rectification (not abandonment), and the distance must not exceed two rows in a congregation or the sutra when alone.
Excuses like narrow space or forgetfulness prevent invalidation.
4
Examine rare external causes
Events like a wasp sting or falling brick are debated: most Hanafis disallow building due to rarity, but Abu Yusuf allows it because it is not one's own act.
The correct view is disallowing building for rare events.
5
Note the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that building is allowed for unintentional hadath, but the preferred precaution is to restart the prayer to avoid disagreement.
This is based on consensus and exit from ikhtilaf.

Source Text
