The Duration of Awrah Exposure or Impurity That Invalidates Prayer
Explains invalidity conditions related to awrah and najasa during rukn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a rukn performed while awrah is exposed or with najasa invalidates the prayer only if the exposure lasts for the duration of a rukn (three tasbihat), and distinguish scenarios based on quantity of exposure and time.

Core Idea
Prayer is not invalidated by momentary exposure; it is the duration of a rukn that matters.

Many assume that any uncovering of the awrah or presence of impurity instantly breaks the prayer. The classical Hanafi position, as clarified by al-Tahtawi in his Hashiyah, introduces a critical nuance: the prayer remains valid if the issue is resolved immediately. The key factor is the time elapsed while performing an integral (rukn) of the prayer. This lesson unpacks the precise measure of that time and the chosen view within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for invalidation
The text states that performing a rukn while awrah is uncovered or with najasa invalidates the prayer, but with a time qualification. Understand that it is not the mere presence but the duration that matters.
The condition is the persistence of the exposure/impurity through the performance of a rukn.
2
Determine the measure of time
The passage defines the relevant time as that which allows performing a rukn with its sunnah, i.e., three tasbihat (saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal-'Azim' or 'Subhana Rabbiyal-A'la' thrice). This is the view of Abu Yusuf and the chosen (mukhtar) position.
The measure is not a fixed number of seconds but the customary duration of a rukn with its recommended parts.
3
Distinguish the four scenarios
The text lists four combinations of quantity of exposure/impurity and time: (1) much in much time – harmful; (2) little in little time – not harmful; (3) much in little time – not harmful; (4) little in much time – harmful. Recognize that harm depends on duration, not quantity alone.
This nuance prevents unnecessary invalidation of prayer.
4
Apply the immediate remedy rule
If the impurity is removed or the awrah is covered immediately upon occurrence (e.g., wind uncovering), and the exposure does not continue for the time of a rukn, the prayer is valid. The text confirms: 'If he removes the impurity immediately... it does not harm him.'
Immediate means without delay, such that no rukn is performed in that state.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The text attributes this time threshold to Imam Abu Yusuf (the second) and states it is the chosen view. This implies a difference with Imam Abu Hanifa, who reportedly considered any exposure invalid. The mufta bihi follows Abu Yusuf.
Knowing the ikhtilaf helps in understanding the school's evolution and providing fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كركوع (أو إمكانه أي مضى زمن يسع أداء ركن (مع كشف العورة أو مع نجاسة مانعة) لوجود المنافي فإن دفع النجاسة بمجرد وقعها ولا أثر لها، أو ستر عورته بمجرد كشفها فلا يضره. قوله: (زمن يسع أداء ركن) وإن كان في ركن طويل، والمراد أنه يسعه بسنته، وهو قدر ثلاث تسبيحات، وهذا مذهب الثاني، وهو المختار كما في الدر قوله : (مع كشف العورة) الحاصل أن الكشف الكثير في الزمن الكثير مضر، والقليل في القليل غير مضر كالكثير في القليل، والقليل في الكثير والمراد بكشف العورة ما. کشف العضو منها . قوله : (أو مع نجاسة مانعة ولو سهو أو تأتي الصور المذكورة في الكشف هنا. قوله: (أو ستر عورته الخ) كأن هبت الريح فكشفته فستر عورته من ساعته فلا يضره
Like bowing (or the possibility of it, i.e., the passage of time that allows performing a integral [of prayer] with uncovering of the awrah or with an impurity that prevents [validity]) because the existence of a contradiction. So if he removes the impurity immediately upon its occurrence and it leaves no trace, or he covers his awrah immediately upon its uncovering, it does not harm him. His statement: 'time that allows performing an integral' even if it is in a long integral, and the intent is that it suffices with its sunnah, which is the measure of three tasbihat, and this is the madhhab of the second [i.e., Abu Yusuf], and it is the chosen view as in al-Durr. His statement: 'with uncovering of the awrah' the summary is that much uncovering in much time is harmful, and little in little time is not harmful, also much in little time [is not harmful] and little in much time [is harmful]. And what is meant by uncovering of the awrah is the uncovering of the limb itself. His statement: 'or with an impurity that prevents' even if by forgetfulness; and the mentioned images for uncovering apply here too. His statement: 'or he covers his awrah etc.' as if the wind blows and uncovers him, so he covers his awrah immediately, it does not harm him.

Commentary
This passage explains the invalidation of prayer when one performs an obligatory action (rukun) while the awrah (private parts) is uncovered or while carrying an impurity (najasa) that prevents validity. The key point is the duration: if the time that elapses is sufficient to perform a rukn (e.g., bowing or prostration) while the awrah is exposed or najasa is present, the prayer becomes invalid. However, if one immediately removes the impurity or covers the awrah as soon as it occurs, and the action does not extend for the duration of a rukn, the prayer is not harmed. The measure of a 'sufficient time' is defined as the time it takes to perform a rukn with its sunnah, i.e., three tasbihat (subhana rabbiyal-'azim or subhana rabbiyal-a'la). This is the view of Imam Abu Yusuf (the 'second') and the chosen (mukhtar) view. The passage also distinguishes between the quantity of uncovering/impurity and time: much uncovering in much time is harmful; little uncovering in little time is not harmful; much in little time is also not harmful; little in much time is harmful. The examples given (wind uncovering the awrah, immediate covering) illustrate the principle that the key is the duration of exposure relative to the time needed for a rukn.

Key Terms
العورة (al-'awrah): The body parts that must be covered during prayer according to Hanafi fiqh
النجاسة المانعة (al-najasah al-mani'ah): An impurity that prevents the validity of prayer, i.e., that is not excused (like heavy impurity on clothes/body)
الركن (al-rukn): An obligatory integral of prayer; if omitted intentionally, prayer is invalid

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the measure of time that, if awrah remains exposed during it, invalidates the prayer?
A) The time of three tasbihat
B) The time of one tasbih
C) The time of one rakah
D) The time of one minute

Key Takeaway
The validity of prayer during awrah exposure or impurity depends on whether the condition persists for the duration of a rukn (three tasbihat); immediate remedy preserves validity.

Preceding the Imam in an Integral Action
Explains invalidity when follower precedes imam in an integral

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scenarios where a muqtadi's prayer becomes invalid due to preceding the imam, and determine the number of make-up rak'ahs required in each case.

Core Idea
Preceding the imam in any integral invalidates unless corrected; make-up rak'ahs vary by pattern.

In congregational prayer, the follower (muqtadi) must synchronize with the imam. But what happens if you accidentally bow or prostrate before the imam? This lesson from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains that such preceding invalidates the prayer if left uncorrected, and details five specific scenarios from al-Asl that determine how many make-up rak'ahs are required. Understanding these nuances helps ensure your prayer remains valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the muqtadi performing a rukn (e.g., ruku or sujud) before the imam. The ruling: if the muqtadi does not repeat the action with or after the imam, the prayer is invalid.
This is the basic rule before considering scenarios.
2
Locate the dalil – why is preceding prohibited?
The proof is qiyas: the imam is appointed to be followed (based on the hadith 'The imam is appointed to be followed'). Preceding breaks this obligation, analogous to breaking a condition of prayer.
Qiyas jali: the 'illa is violating the duty to follow.
3
Explore the first scenario – preceding in all rak'ahs without ending with imam
If the muqtadi does not give salam with the imam and precedes in ruku and sujud in all rak'ahs, he performs one make-up rak'ah after the imam, without recitation. He is considered mudrik (catches the first part) but missed the first rak'ah due to not following.
Each subsequent rak'ah's actions serve as qada for the previous missed rak'ah.
4
Analyze the branching from al-Asl – five scenarios
Al-Asl details five patterns based on the timing of bowing and prostrating relative to the imam. For example, bowing with the imam but prostrating before him requires two make-up rak'ahs; bowing before and prostrating requires four; bowing and prostrating after the imam is valid.
The text enumerates these as five scenarios, including the one from the main text.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The number of required make-up rak'ahs differs: 1, 2, 4, or none depending on the pattern. This affects the muqtadi's post-prayer actions.
The rule is intricate; the muqtadi must carefully evaluate his actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يفسدها (مسابقة المقتدي بركن لم يشاركه فيه (إمامه كما لو ركع ورفع رأسه قبل الإمام، ولم يعده معه أو بعده وسلم، وإذا لم يسلم مع الإمام وسابقه بالركوع والسجود في كل الركعات قضى ركعة بلا قراءة لأنه مدرك أول صلاة الإمام لا حق، وهو يقضي قبل فراغ الإمام وقد فاتته الركعة الأولى بتركه متابعة الإمام في الركوع والسجود، فيكون ركوعه وسجوده في الثانية قضاء عن الأولى، وفي الثالثة عن الثانية وفي الرابعة عن الثالثة فيقضي بعده ركعة بغير قراءة وتمام تفريعه بالأصل) أي في الأصل قال فيه : وإن ركع مع إمامه، وسجد قبله لزمه قضاء ركعتين لأنه يلتحق سجدتاه في الثانية بركوعه في الأولى لأنه كان معتبراً ويلغو ركوعه في الثانية لوقوعه عقب ركوعه الأول بلا سجود، ثم ركوعه في الثالثة مع الإمام معتبر دون ركوعه في الرابعة لكونه قبل سجوده، فيلتحق به سجوده في رابعة الإمام فيصير عليه الثانية والرابعة فيقضيهما، وإن ركع قبل إمامه، وسجد يقضي أربعاً بلا قراءة لأن السجود لا يعتد به إذا لم يتقدمه ركوع صحيح، وركوعه في كل الركعات قبل الإمام يبطل سجوده الحاصل معه، وإما إن ركع إمامه وسجد، ثم ركع وسجد بعده جازت صلاته، فهذه خمس صور مأخوذة من فتح القدير، والخلاصة والمراد أنها خمسة بما في المصنف
And it invalidates it: the follower preceding [the imam] in an integral in which the imam does not share with him, as if he bowed and raised his head before the imam, and did not repeat it with him or after him, and he [the imam] gave salam. And if he does not give salam with the imam and he precedes him in bowing and prostrating in all the rak'ahs, he performs one rak'ah as a make-up without recitation, because he is idrak of the first part of the imam's prayer, not a lahiq, and he performs the make-up before the imam finishes. The first rak'ah was missed by leaving the following of the imam in ruku and sujud. So his ruku and sujud in the second [rak'ah] are a make-up for the first, in the third for the second, and in the fourth for the third. So he performs one rak'ah after him without recitation. The complete branching of this is in the Asl. In the Asl it is said: if he bowed with his imam and prostrated before him, it is incumbent on him to perform two rak'ahs make-up, because his two prostrations in the second rak'ah attach to his bowing in the first, because it was considered valid, and his bowing in the second is annulled because it occurred after his first bowing without prostration. Then his bowing in the third with the imam is considered, but not his bowing in the fourth because it was before his prostration, so his prostration in the imam's fourth attaches to it. So the second and fourth are due on him, and he makes them up. If he bowed before his imam and prostrated, he performs four [rak'ahs] make-up without recitation, because prostration is not considered valid if not preceded by a valid bowing, and his bowing in all the rak'ahs before the imam invalidates his prostration that occurred with him. And if his imam bowed and prostrated, and then he bowed and prostrated after him, his prayer is valid. So these are five scenarios taken from Fath al-Qadir, and the summary is that they are five including that which is in the text.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi discusses the invalidation of prayer when a follower (muqtadi) precedes the imam in performing an obligatory action (rukn). The basic ruling: if the bowing and raising before the imam and does not repeat it, the prayer is invalid. Then it details a specific scenario: if the follower does not end his prayer with the imam (by giving salam) but rather precedes him in ruku and sujud throughout all rak'ahs, then he performs one additional rak'ah after the imam as a make-up (qada), without recitation. The reason is that he is considered 'mudrik' of the first part of the imam's prayer, not 'lahiq' (one who catches up later). The first rak'ah is missed, so the actions in the subsequent rak'ahs serve as makeup for the missed ones. The 'Asl' (al-Asl, the foundational work by Imam Muhammad) provides detailed branching into five scenarios based on the sequence of bowing and prostrating relative to the imam. For example, if the follower bows with the imam but prostrates before him, he must perform two rak'ahs make-up; if he bows before the imam and then prostrates, he must perform four rak'ahs make-up. If he bows and prostrates after the imam, the prayer is valid. These scenarios illustrate the intricate Hanafi rules regarding following the imam in congregational prayer.

Key Terms
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The person following the imam in congregational prayer
المسابقة (al-musabaqah): The act of preceding the imam in a prayer action
القضاء (al-qada'): Make-up prayer performed after the imam's salam to compensate for missed or invalid actions

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is valid but disliked.
B) The prayer is invalid.
C) He must perform additional sajdah al-sahw.
D) His prayer is valid but must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Preceding the imam in an integral action invalidates the prayer unless the action is repeated after the imam; the number of make-up rak'ahs depends on the specific pattern of preceding.

Masbuq Following Imam in Sajdat al-Sahw After Becoming Independent
Ruling on invalidity of masbuq following imam in sajdat al-sahw after independence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that a masbuq's prayer is invalid if he follows the imam in sajdat al-sahw after confirming independence, and identify the conditions that define independence.

Core Idea
Once a masbuq becomes independent (infirad), following the imam in sajdat al-sahw invalidates his prayer.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in congregational prayer: the latecomer (masbuq) who, after completing his missed rak'ahs and becoming independent, mistakenly follows the imam in the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw). The Hanafi school rules that such action invalidates the prayer entirely. Understanding what constitutes independence is crucial to avoid this error.

Guided Path
1
Identify the status of the masbuq
A masbuq is one who misses one or more rak'ahs of congregational prayer. After the imam's salam, the masbuq stands to complete his missed rak'ahs. At a certain point, he becomes independent (munfarid) from the imam.
The masbuq is considered a follower (muqtadi) until he signals independence by standing for his own rak'ahs.
2
Determine the moment of independence (infirad)
Independence is confirmed when the masbuq either stands after the imam's salam or, if he stood earlier, after sitting for the duration of tashahhud and then standing again. The text specifically mentions 'his sitting of the measure of tashahhud' as a key marker.
Performing one prostration (sajdah) after standing is also mentioned as part of tying his rak'ah.
3
Recognize the invalidity of following after independence
If after confirming independence the imam performs sajdat al-sahw and the masbuq follows him, his prayer becomes invalid. The reason is that he has re-entered the state of being a follower after being independent, which is not permitted.
The ruling applies only if the masbuq's independence is firmly established; if he is still in a borderline state, the prayer may remain valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يفسدها متعابة الإمام في سجود السهو للمسبوق) إذا تأكد انفراده بأن قام بعد سلام الإمام أو قبله بعد قعوده قدر التشهد، وقيد ركعته بسجدة فتذكر الإمام سجود سهو فتابعه فسدت صلاته لأنه اقتدى بعد وجود الانفراد، قوله: (للمسبوق) أي المتابعة الثابتة للمسبوق، والأولى كما قاله السيد: أن يقول : متابعة المسبوق الإمام في سجود السهو قوله : ( وقيد ركعته بسجدة) أما إذا
And it invalidates it: the following of the imam in the prostration of forgetfulness by the one who is preceded [masbuq], when his independence is confirmed, such that he stood after the imam's salam or before it after his sitting of the measure of tashahhud, and he tied his rak'ah with a single prostration; then the imam remembered a prostration of forgetfulness, and he [the masbuq] followed him, so his prayer is invalid, because he followed after the existence of independence. His statement: 'for the masbuq' meaning the following that is established for the masbuq, and it is better, as al-Sayyid said, to say: the following of the masbuq of the imam in the prostration of forgetfulness. His statement: 'and he tied his rak'ah with a single prostration' as for if...
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific scenario in prayer: a latecomer (masbuq) who, after completing his missed rak'ahs and becoming independent (infirad), follows the imam in the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw). The ruling is that if the masbuq has already become independent (by standing after the imam's salam or after sitting for the tashahhud), and he ties his rak'ah with a single prostration, then if the imam remembers a sajdat al-sahw and the masbuq follows him, his prayer becomes invalid. The reason is that he has re-entered the congregation after being independent, which is not allowed. The passage clarifies that the 'following' referred to is the specific following of the masbuq of the imam in sajdat al-sahw. The text is cut off at 'as for if...' which would likely discuss the exception where the action is permissible. This ruling guards against the error of a masbuq mistakenly reverting to following the imam after his own prayer has become separate.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer who misses one or more rak'ahs of the congregational prayer and completes them after the imam's salam
الانفراد (al-infirad): The state of becoming independent from the imam after completing the missed part
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Two prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for forgetfulness

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A masbuq must not follow the imam in sajdat al-sahw after independence is confirmed, as it invalidates the prayer.

Invalidity When Follower Precedes Imam in a Pillar: Basic Ruling
Ruling on follower preceding imam in a pillar and its consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a follower races ahead of the imam in a pillar and identify when the prayer becomes invalid or requires qada.

Core Idea
If the follower precedes the imam in a pillar and does not repeat it, his prayer is invalid.

The follower's prayer is invalid if he performs a pillar before the imam and does not correct it. This lesson explains the basic case and a variant where the follower races ahead in all rak'ahs but does not say salam with the imam, leading to a qada of one rak'ah without recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Determine that the follower (muqtadi) performs a pillar, such as ruku' or sujud, before the imam.
This is called musabaqah (racing ahead).
2
Check for correction
Did the follower repeat the pillar with or after the imam? If he did not, the prayer becomes invalid (fasid).
The text states: 'If he bows and raises his head before the imam, and does not repeat it with him or after him and says salam, the prayer is invalid.'
3
Consider the variant
If the follower races ahead in all rak'ahs but does not say salam with the imam, he is considered a mudrik (perceiver of the whole prayer) and must perform one rak'ah qada after the imam's salam without recitation.
This is because the first rak'ah was lost due to missing following in all its pillars.
4
Note the salam condition
If the follower says salam with the imam after racing ahead, the prayer is invalid immediately because he deliberately ended based on a false completion.
This is clearly distinguished: salam with imam → invalid; no salam → qada of one rak'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يفسدها (مسابقة المقتدي بركن لم يشاركه فيه (إمامه كما لو ركع ورفع رأسه قبل الإمام، ولم يعده معه أو بعده وسلم، وإذا لم يسلم مع الإمام وسابقه بالركوع والسجود في كل الركعات قضى ركعة بلا قراءة لأنه مدرك أول صلاة الإمام لا حق، وهو يقضي قبل فراغ الإمام وقد فاتته الركعة الأولى بتركه متابعة الإمام في الركوع والسجود، فيكون ركوعه وسجوده في الثانية قضاء عن الأولى، وفي الثالثة عن الثانية وفي الرابعة عن الثالثة فيقضي بعده ركعة بغير قراءة وتمام تفريعه بالأصل) قوله: (وإذا لم يسلم مع الإمام الخ) أما لو سلم معه فسدت صلاته لأنه سلم عمد أبناء على أنه أتمها. قوله: (لأنه مدرك الخ) روح العلة. قوله: (وهو يقضي قبل فراغ الإمام أي حتماً إن أمكنه إدراكه. قوله: (فيقضي بعده ركعة) أي بعد سلام الإمام، والأولى التصريح به. قوله: (وتمام تفريعه بالأصل) أي في الأصل قال فيه: وإن ركع مع إمامه، وسجد قبله لزمه قضاء ركعتين لأنه يلتحق سجدتاه في الثانية بركوعه في الأولى لأنه كان معتبراً ويلغو ركوعه في الثانية لوقوعه عقب ركوعه الأول بلا سجود، ثم ركوعه في الثالثة مع الإمام معتبر دون ركوعه في الرابعة لكونه قبل سجوده، فيلتحق به سجوده في رابعة الإمام فيصير عليه الثانية والرابعة فيقضيهما، وإن ركع قبل إمامه، وسجد يقضي أربعاً بلا قراءة لأن السجود لا يعتد به إذا لم يتقدمه ركوع صحيح، وركوعه في كل الركعات قبل الإمام يبطل سجوده الحاصل معه، وإما إن ركع إمامه وسجد، ثم ركع وسجد بعده جازت صلاته، فهذه خمس صور مأخوذة من فتح القدير، والخلاصة والمراد أنها خمسة بما في المصنف
(And) invalidates it (the prayer) the follower racing ahead in a pillar he does not share with his imam, like if he bows and raises his head before the imam, and does not repeat it with him or after him and says salam. And if he does not say salam with the imam and races ahead in bowing and prostrating in all rak'ahs, he performs one rak'ah without recitation because he is a perceiver (mudrik) of the first part of the imam's prayer, not a latecomer, and he makes it up before the imam finishes, and the first rak'ah is lost because he left following the imam in bowing and prostrating. So his bowing and prostration in the second (rak'ah) is qada for the first, and in the third for the second, and in the fourth for the third, so he performs one rak'ah after him without recitation. His saying: (And if he does not say salam with the imam etc.) But if he says salam with him, his prayer is invalid because he deliberately said salam based on thinking he had completed. His saying: (Because he is a mudrik etc.) is the spirit of the cause. His saying: (And he makes it up before the imam finishes) means definitively if possible. His saying: (So he performs one rak'ah after him) means after the imam's salam, and it is clearer to express that. His saying: (And the complete derivation of its branches is in al-Asl) means in al-Asl he said: If he bows with his imam and prostrates before him, he owes qada of two rak'ahs because his prostrations in the second are attached to his bowing in the first because it was considered, and his bowing in the second is void because it occurs after his first bowing without prostration. And if his imam bowed and prostrated, then he bows and prostrates after him, his prayer is valid. Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn commented upon by al-Tahtawi regarding a specific invalidator of prayer: when the follower (muqtadi) performs a pillar (like ruku' or sujud) before the imam and does not repeat it with him or after him. The basic case is if the follower bows and rises before the imam, does not repeat the bowing, and then says salam, the prayer is invalid. The hashiya then explains a more complex scenario where a latecomer (masbuq) who realizes he missed the first rak'ah? Actually the text says 'إذا لم يسلم مع الإمام' - if he does not say salam with the imam but races ahead in all rak'ahs. This is about a person who is mudrik (perceiving the entire prayer) but still races ahead. The ruling is that he owes one rak'ah qada after the imam's salam without recitation. The hashiya clarifies the reasoning: he is considered mudrik, not lahiq (one who missed part). Then the hashiya cites al-Asl (the work of Imam Muhammad) which outlines five cases with detailed rules for different scenarios of bowing and prostrating out of order between the follower and imam. These five cases are summarized from Fath al-Qadir and al-Khulasa. The overall principle is that the follower must not precede the imam in any pillar; if he does, his prayer is invalid unless he corrects it properly.

Key Terms
مسابقة (musabaqah): The follower racing ahead of the imam in performing a pillar, which invalidates prayer unless corrected.
مقتدي (muqtadi): A follower who joins the imam from the beginning of the prayer (mudrik) or later (masbuq). Here it refers to a follower in general.
لحق (lahiq): A latecomer who misses part of the prayer and must make it up after the imam's salam.

Key Takeaway
A follower must not precede the imam in any pillar; if he does and does not correct, the prayer is invalid.

Detailed Cases from al-Asl: Five Scenarios of Follower and Imam Timing
Five specific cases of follower's timing relative to imam from al-Asl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings to five specific scenarios where the follower's bowing and prostration timing relative to the imam determines validity or qada.

Core Idea
If follower bows with imam but prostrates before him, he owes two rak'ahs qada; if he bows before imam and prostrates, he owes four; if he follows correctly, prayer is valid.

Al-Tahtawi cites al-Asl for five detailed scenarios that extend the basic ruling on musabaqah. Each scenario involves different timing of ruku' and sujud between the follower and imam, resulting in different qada requirements or validity.

Guided Path
1
Familiarize with the five scenarios
The text from al-Asl outlines five cases: (1) basic musabaqah with salam, (2) bow with imam, prostrate before, (3) bow before imam, prostrate after, (4) bow before, prostrate before, (5) correct following (imam bows first, follower follows).
Scenario (1) is the basic case covered in Lesson 1; scenarios (2)-(5) are detailed here.
2
Analyze each scenario
For each, identify the timing of ruku' and sujud relative to the imam. Determine if the follower's actions are valid or require qada.
Key principle: a valid prostration must be preceded by a valid bowing (ruku').
3
Determine the outcome
Scenario (2): bow with imam, prostrate before → qada of two rak'ahs. Scenario (3): bow before imam, prostrate after → qada of four rak'ahs. Scenario (4): bow before and prostrate before → qada of four rak'ahs (since bowing before imam invalidates subsequent prostration). Scenario (5): imam bows and prostrates first, follower follows → valid.
The number of qada rak'ahs depends on how many pillars are missed due to the timing.
4
Apply the rulings
Given a new scenario not explicitly mentioned, use the principles to deduce the ruling. For example, if follower bows after imam but prostrates before, it would be similar to scenario (2) but with bowing after, which might be valid? Actually, bowing after imam is correct; premature prostration is invalid.
Always check the sequence: bowing before imam invalidates all subsequent prostration in that rak'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يفسدها (مسابقة المقتدي بركن لم يشاركه فيه (إمامه كما لو ركع ورفع رأسه قبل الإمام، ولم يعده معه أو بعده وسلم، وإذا لم يسلم مع الإمام وسابقه بالركوع والسجود في كل الركعات قضى ركعة بلا قراءة لأنه مدرك أول صلاة الإمام لا حق، وهو يقضي قبل فراغ الإمام وقد فاتته الركعة الأولى بتركه متابعة الإمام في الركوع والسجود، فيكون ركوعه وسجوده في الثانية قضاء عن الأولى، وفي الثالثة عن الثانية وفي الرابعة عن الثالثة فيقضي بعده ركعة بغير قراءة وتمام تفريعه بالأصل) قوله: (وإذا لم يسلم مع الإمام الخ) أما لو سلم معه فسدت صلاته لأنه سلم عمد أبناء على أنه أتمها. قوله: (لأنه مدرك الخ) روح العلة. قوله: (وهو يقضي قبل فراغ الإمام أي حتماً إن أمكنه إدراكه. قوله: (فيقضي بعده ركعة) أي بعد سلام الإمام، والأولى التصريح به. قوله: (وتمام تفريعه بالأصل) أي في الأصل قال فيه: وإن ركع مع إمامه، وسجد قبله لزمه قضاء ركعتين لأنه يلتحق سجدتاه في الثانية بركوعه في الأولى لأنه كان معتبراً ويلغو ركوعه في الثانية لوقوعه عقب ركوعه الأول بلا سجود، ثم ركوعه في الثالثة مع الإمام معتبر دون ركوعه في الرابعة لكونه قبل سجوده، فيلتحق به سجوده في رابعة الإمام فيصير عليه الثانية والرابعة فيقضيهما، وإن ركع قبل إمامه، وسجد يقضي أربعاً بلا قراءة لأن السجود لا يعتد به إذا لم يتقدمه ركوع صحيح، وركوعه في كل الركعات قبل الإمام يبطل سجوده الحاصل معه، وإما إن ركع إمامه وسجد، ثم ركع وسجد بعده جازت صلاته، فهذه خمس صور مأخوذة من فتح القدير، والخلاصة والمراد أنها خمسة بما في المصنف
(And) invalidates it (the prayer) the follower racing ahead in a pillar he does not share with his imam, like if he bows and raises his head before the imam, and does not repeat it with him or after him and says salam. And if he does not say salam with the imam and races ahead in bowing and prostrating in all rak'ahs, he performs one rak'ah without recitation because he is a perceiver (mudrik) of the first part of the imam's prayer, not a latecomer, and he makes it up before the imam finishes, and the first rak'ah is lost because he left following the imam in bowing and prostrating. So his bowing and prostration in the second (rak'ah) is qada for the first, and in the third for the second, and in the fourth for the third, so he performs one rak'ah after him without recitation. And the complete derivation of its branches is in al-Asl. His saying: (And if he does not say salam with the imam etc.) But if he says salam with him, his prayer is invalid because he deliberately said salam based on thinking he had completed. His saying: (Because he is a mudrik etc.) is the spirit of the cause. His saying: (And he makes it up before the imam finishes) means definitively if possible. His saying: (So he performs one rak'ah after him) means after the imam's salam, and it is clearer to express that. His saying: (And the complete derivation of its branches is in al-Asl) means in al-Asl he said: If he bows with his imam and prostrates before him, he owes qada of two rak'ahs because his prostrations in the second are attached to his bowing in the first because it was considered, and his bowing in the second is void because it occurs after his first bowing without prostration. Then his bowing in the third with the imam is considered, not his bowing in the fourth because it is before his prostration, so his prostration in the fourth of the imam attaches to it, so the second and fourth become due upon him, so he performs them as qada. And if he bows before his imam and prostrates, he performs four rak'ahs without recitation because the prostration is not considered if not preceded by a valid bowing, and his bowing in all rak'ahs before the imam nullifies his prostration done with him. And if his imam bowed and prostrated, then he bows and prostrates after him, his prayer is valid. These are five cases taken from Fath al-Qadir and al-Khulasa, and it is meant that they are five including what is in the matn.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn commented upon by al-Tahtawi regarding a specific invalidator of prayer: when the follower (muqtadi) performs a pillar (like ruku' or sujud) before the imam and does not repeat it with him or after him. The basic case is if the follower bows and rises before the imam, does not repeat the bowing, and then says salam, the prayer is invalid. The hashiya then explains a more complex scenario where a latecomer (masbuq) who realizes he missed the first rak'ah? Actually the text says 'إذا لم يسلم مع الإمام' - if he does not say salam with the imam but races ahead in all rak'ahs. This is about a person who is mudrik (perceiving the entire prayer) but still races ahead. The ruling is that he owes one rak'ah qada after the imam's salam without recitation. The hashiya clarifies the reasoning: he is considered mudrik, not lahiq (one who missed part). Then the hashiya cites al-Asl (the work of Imam Muhammad) which outlines five cases with detailed rules for different scenarios of bowing and prostrating out of order between the follower and imam. These five cases are summarized from Fath al-Qadir and al-Khulasa. The overall principle is that the follower must not precede the imam in any pillar; if he does, his prayer is invalid unless he corrects it properly.

Key Terms
مسابقة (musabaqah): The follower racing ahead of the imam in performing a pillar.
قضاء (qada): Making up missed rak'ahs after the imam's salam without recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One rak'ah
B) Two rak'ahs
C) Four rak'ahs
D) The prayer is valid

Key Takeaway
The timing of ruku' and sujud relative to the imam determines whether the prayer is valid or requires qada; bowing validity is key.

Masbuq Following Imam in Sajdah Sahw After Separation
Ruling on the invalidity of the masbuq's prayer if he follows the imam in sajdah sahw after having tied his rak'ah with a sajda

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios that invalidate a masbuq's prayer and apply the condition regarding tying the rak'ah with a sajda.

Core Idea
A masbuq who ties his rak'ah must not follow the imam in sajdah sahw; doing so invalidates.

In congregational prayer, the masbuq (latecomer) has a special status: he follows the imam in what remains and then completes his missed rak'ahs. However, once he has 'tied his rak'ah with a sajdah' (meaning he has performed a prostration for that rak'ah and become independent), he must not re-join the imam for sajdah sahw. The Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies that doing so invalidates his prayer. Additionally, a masbuq should not stand to pray his own rak'ahs before the imam has sat for the duration of tashahhud; otherwise, his prayer is invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the masbuq's status
The masbuq joins the prayer late and follows the imam in the remaining parts, then completes his own missed rak'ahs.
2
Define 'tying the rak'ah with a sajda'
This means the masbuq has performed a sajda for his current rak'ah, indicating independence from the imam's current rak'ah.
It marks the completion of a full rak'ah for that unit.
3
Apply the ruling on sajdah sahw
If the masbuq has tied his rak'ah and then follows the imam in sajdah sahw, his prayer becomes invalid (fasid).
He should not rejoin the imam after becoming independent.
4
Note the additional condition on standing
The masbuq must not stand for his own rak'ahs before the imam has sat for tashahhud; if he does, his prayer is invalid.
The imam still owes an obligation that the masbuq cannot fulfill alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (للمسبوق) أي المتابعة الثابتة للمسبوق، والأولى كما قاله السيد: أن يقول : متابعة المسبوق الإمام في سجود السهو. قوله : ( وقيد ركعته بسجدة) أما إذا قيد ركعته بسجدة فتفسد صلاته، وقيدنا قيام المسبوق بكونه بعد قعود الإمام قدر التشهد لأنه إن كان قبله لم يجزء لأن الإمام بقي عليه فرض لا ينفرد به المسبوق فتفسد صلاته
His saying: (For the masbuq) meaning the established following for the masbuq, and it is better as al-Sayyid said to say: the masbuq following the imam in sajdah sahw. His saying: (And he tied his rak'ah with a sajda) but if he tied his rak'ah with a sajda, then his prayer becomes invalid. And we have restricted the standing of the masbuq to being after the sitting of the imam to the extent of tashahhud, because if it was before that, it is not sufficient because the imam still has an obligation due upon him which the masbuq cannot perform alone, and thus his prayer becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage from the hashiya explains the ruling on the masbuq (latecomer) following the imam in the sajdah sahw (prostration for forgetfulness). The matn states that the prayer is invalid if the masbuq follows the imam in sajdah sahw after having established his independence. The hashiya clarifies that 'establishing independence' means the masbuq has tied his rak'ah with a sajda, i.e., he has performed a sajda for that rak'ah, which indicates he has separated from the imam's current rak'ah. If he then follows the imam in sajdah sahw, his prayer is invalid because he is re-joining the imam after having become independent. The hashiya also notes a condition: the masbuq's standing (to perform his own rak'ahs) must occur after the imam has sat for the duration of tashahhud. If the masbuq stands before that, it is not valid because the imam still owes an obligation (the remainder of the prayer) that the masbuq cannot fulfill alone, so the masbuq's prayer is invalid. This is a nuanced ruling about the timing of separation in congregational prayer.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregational prayer late, missing one or more rak'ahs.
سجود السهو (sujood al-sahw): Prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
قيد ركعته بسجدة (qayyada rak'atahu bi-sajdah): The act of tying one's rak'ah by performing a prostration, meaning the masbuq has completed a full rak'ah and is no longer following the imam's current rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only if he has tied his rak'ah with a sajda (established independence)
C) Only if he has not tied his rak'ah with a sajda
D) Never, the masbuq must always follow the imam

Key Takeaway
The masbuq's prayer becomes fasid if he follows the imam in sajdah sahw after tying his rak'ah with a sajda, and also if he stands before the imam's tashahhud sitting.

The Invalidity of Not Repeating the Final Sitting After a Post-Sitting Sajda
Ruling on not repeating final sitting after a sajda remembered post-sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that not repeating the final sitting after performing a sajda (salibiyya or tilawah) remembered after the sitting invalidates the prayer, and explain the basis for the chosen view (mukhtar).

Core Idea
A sajda after the final sitting overturns it; the sitting must be repeated or the prayer is invalid.

One of the subtle invalidators of prayer is failing to repeat the final sitting after performing a sajda—whether a missed regular sajda (salibiyya) or a tilawah sajda—that is remembered only after one has already sat for the final tashahhud. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the reasoning behind it, including an intra-Hanafi difference of opinion on whether sajda tilawah overturns the sitting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing a sajda (either a regular sajda of the prayer or a tilawah sajda) after the final sitting. The ruling is that the final sitting is overturned and must be repeated; if not repeated, the prayer becomes fasid (invalid).
Focus on the invalidity condition: failure to repeat the sitting.
2
Understand the rationale
The final sitting is only valid after all pillars (arkan) are completed. Performing an extra sajda after the sitting disrupts this order, so the sitting is no longer valid and must be redone.
The text says: 'because the final sitting is not considered valid except after completion of the pillars'.
3
Recognize the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
There is disagreement on whether sajda tilawah overturns the final sitting. According to the chosen view (al-mukhtar), it does; some scholars (e.g., Shams al-A'imma) say it does not because sajda tilawah is wajib, not fard, and a wajib does not overturn a fard (the final sitting is a pillar).
The hashiya explicitly mentions 'al-mukhtar'.
4
Apply the ruling
In practice, if you remember a missed sajda or are required to perform sajda tilawah after the final sitting, perform the sajda and then repeat the final sitting. Without repeating, your prayer is invalid.
This applies to both sajda salibiyya and tilawah according to the chosen view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يفسدها (عدم إعادة الجلوس الأخير بعد أداء سجدة صلبية أو سجدة تلاوة (تذكرها بعد الجلوس) لأنه لا يعتد بالجلوس الأخير إلا بعد تمام الأركان لأنه لختمها ولا تعارض ولارتفاض الأخير بسجدة التلاوة على المختار (و) يفسدها (عدم إعادة ركن أداه نائما) لأن شرط صحته أداؤه مستيقظاً كما تقدم
(And) invalidates it (the prayer) not repeating the final sitting after performing a sajda of the prayer or a sajda of tilawah (remembering it after the sitting) because the final sitting is not considered valid except after completion of the pillars, because it is for sealing the prayer and there is no contradiction, and the final (sitting) is overturned by the sajda of tilawah according to the chosen view. (And) invalidates it (not repeating a pillar performed while sleeping) because the condition for its validity is to perform it while awake, as previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage lists two additional invalidators of prayer. The first: if a person performs a sajda (either a sajda of the prayer itself, like a forgotten sajda, or a sajda of tilawah) and remembers it after having already sat for the final tashahhud, he must repeat the final sitting; failure to do so invalidates the prayer. The reason is that the final sitting is only valid after all pillars are completed; performing an extra sajda after the sitting disrupts the sitting, so it must be redone. The hashiya notes that according to the chosen view (al-mukhtar), the final sitting is overturned by sajda tilawah. The second invalidator: if a person performs a pillar (e.g., ruku' or sujud) while sleeping (unconscious or asleep), and then does not repeat that pillar after waking up, the prayer is invalid because the condition for a valid pillar is that it is performed while conscious. This ruling was mentioned earlier in the text.

Key Terms
سجدة صلبية (sajdah salibiyyah): A prostration that is part of the prayer itself, such as the sajdah in ruku' or sujud, as opposed to sajdat al-tilawah.
سجدة تلاوة (sajdah tilawah): A prostration performed upon reciting or hearing certain verses of the Quran.
جلوس أخير (julus akhir): The final sitting in prayer after the last prostration, in which tashahhud is recited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen view (mukhtar), what is the effect of performing sajda tilawah after the final sitting?
A) The final sitting remains valid and the prayer is complete.
B) The final sitting is overturned and must be repeated.
C) The prayer becomes invalid without the possibility of correction.
D) The sajda tilawah is not valid after the final sitting.

Key Takeaway
Any sajda performed after the final sitting—whether salibiyya or tilawah—overturns the sitting, requiring its repetition; failure to repeat invalidates the prayer.

The Invalidity of Not Repeating a Pillar Performed While Sleeping
Ruling on not repeating a pillar performed while sleeping

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a pillar (rukn) of prayer performed while sleeping is invalid and must be repeated, and that failure to do so invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
A pillar performed while sleeping is invalid; it must be repeated awake or the prayer is void.

Another invalidator of prayer is performing a pillar (such as ruku' or sujud) while in a state of sleep or unconsciousness, and then not repeating it after waking up. This lesson explains the condition that a valid pillar requires consciousness, and the consequence of omitting its repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing a pillar (rukn) of the prayer while sleeping (nā'im). The ruling is that the prayer is invalid if that pillar is not repeated after waking up.
The text says: 'invalidates it (the prayer) not repeating a pillar performed while sleeping'.
2
Understand the condition of validity
A valid pillar requires the worshipper to be awake and conscious (mustayqiẓ). A sleeping person lacks awareness, so the pillar is not validly performed.
The text: 'because the condition for its validity is to perform it while awake'.
3
Apply the ruling
If you perform a pillar (e.g., sujud) while drowsy or asleep, you must repeat that pillar once you are fully awake. If you do not repeat it, your prayer is invalid.
This applies to all pillars: ruku', sujud, qiyam, etc.

Masbuq Following Imam in Sujud Tilawah
Ruling on masbuq following imam in sujud tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions for when a masbuq must follow the imam in sujud tilawah and state the related intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
A masbuq's obligation to follow in sujud tilawah depends on whether his independence is confirmed — following when independent invalidates his prayer.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies a nuanced area for the masbuq (latecomer) in congregational prayer. Students often assume the masbuq must always follow the imam in sujud tilawah, but the text shows the ruling depends on the masbuq's independence status. We will dissect the two scenarios and determine the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
Determine whether the masbuq has confirmed his independence (ta'akkud infirad) by performing his own sujud for the rak'ah. If yes, he is independent; if no, he is still attached.
Independence is typically confirmed once the masbuq has performed a sajda in his own rak'ah.
2
Ruling when independence is not confirmed
If the masbuq has not confirmed independence (i.e., he has not yet performed his own sujud), he must return and follow the imam in sujud tilawah. If he does not, his prayer is invalid because the imam's sitting is overturned.
In this state, the masbuq's actions are still tied to the imam.
3
Ruling when independence is confirmed
If the masbuq has confirmed independence, there are two narrations: one that his prayer is invalid if he returns, and one that it is invalid if he does not return. The apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) says his prayer is invalid in both cases, and this is the more correct view.
The reasoning is that returning to sujud tilawah after independence overturns the sitting, breaking the required following.
4
Note the exception for sajdah sahw
If the masbuq followed the imam in sajdah sahw and it turns out the imam had no sahw, the later scholars (mutakhkhirin) rule the masbuq's prayer valid. This is separate from sujud tilawah.
The fatwa is upon this lenient view for sajdah sahw.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
For sujud tilawah, the relied-upon (mukhtar) position is that if the masbuq's independence is confirmed, his prayer is invalid whether he returns or not. This is the zahir al-riwaya and the more correct narration.
The later scholars' tarjih strengthens this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من لم يقيد وسجد الإمام وجب متابعته وارتفض ما أداه وإن مضى على صلاته صحت لأن المتابعة واجبة لكونها في واجب، وترك الواجب لا يوجب فساداً، ويسجد للسهو بعد الفراغ قضائه استحساناً، ولو تابع المسبوق إمامه في سجود السهو فتبين أنه لا سهو عليه، فصلاة المسبوق جائزة عند المتأخرين وعليه الفتوى ولو سجد الإمام للتلاوة فإن لم يتأكد انفراد المسبوق عاد حتماً، ولا يعتد بما أدى قبله ولو لم يعد فسدت صلاته لارتفاض القعود في حق الإمام فير تفض في حقه، وإن تأكد انفراده بتقييد الركعة بسجدة فإن عاد فسدت صلاته رواية واحدة، وإن لم يعد ومضى ففيه روايتان وظاهر الرواية الفساد وهو أصح الروايتين لأن العود إلى سجود التلاوة . يرفض القعدة فتبين أن المسبوق إنفرد في موضع الإقتداء فتفسد صلاته
Whoever has not tied (his rak'ah) and the imam prostrated (for tilawah), it is obligatory to follow him and what he performed is overturned, and if he continues his prayer, it is valid because following is obligatory being in an obligatory matter, and leaving an obligatory does not cause invalidity, and he performs sajdah sahw after finishing his qada by istihsan. And if the masbuq followed his imam in sajdah sahw and it turns out that there is no sahw upon him, the masbuq's prayer is valid according to the later scholars and upon it is the fatwa. And if the imam prostrated for tilawah, then if the masbuq's independence is not confirmed he must return, and what he performed before is not considered, and if he does not return, his prayer is invalid because the sitting is overturned in the right of the imam, so it is overturned in his right. And if his independence is confirmed by tying the rak'ah with a sajda, then if he returns, his prayer is invalid in one narration, and if he does not return and continues, there are two narrations: the apparent narration is invalidity, and it is the more correct of the two narrations because returning to sajdat al-tilawah overturns the sitting, and it becomes clear that the masbuq has isolated in a place of following, so his prayer is invalid.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage from the hashiya discusses the rules for the masbuq (latecomer) when the imam performs sujud al-tilawah (prostration of recitation). It distinguishes two scenarios based on whether the masbuq has established independence (ta'akkud infirad) by tying his rak'ah with a sajda. If the masbuq has not yet tied his rak'ah (i.e., he is still in the process of following the imam's current rak'ah), then when the imam prostrates for tilawah, the masbuq must follow him and his previous prayer actions are overturned. If he does not follow, his prayer is invalid because the imam's sitting is overturned, and thus the masbuq's sitting is also overturned. If the masbuq has already tied his rak'ah with a sujud (i.e., he has completed a rak'ah and is independent), then if he returns to follow the imam in sujud tilawah, his prayer is invalid in one narration (riwayah). If he does not return and continues, there are two narrations: the apparent (zahir al-riwaya) is that his prayer is invalid, and this is the more correct opinion. The reasoning is that by returning to sujud tilawah, the masbuq is re-joining the imam after having become independent, which invalidates his prayer. This is a nuanced area with multiple narrations, and the hashiya presents the relied-upon view.

Key Terms
تأكد انفراده (ta'akkud infiradihi): The confirmation of the masbuq's independence from the imam, typically by having performed a sajda for his own rak'ah.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or transmitted narration from the early masters (usually Imam Muhammad), carrying stronger weight in the school.
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing certain Quranic verses; it is wajib in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the masbuq has confirmed his independence (ta'akkud infirad) by tying his rak'ah with a sajda, and the imam performs sujud tilawah, what is the ruling according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) if the masbuq does not return?
A) His prayer is valid
B) His prayer is invalid
C) He must perform sajdah sahw
D) He must repeat the prayer

Key Takeaway
The masbuq's independence (ta'akkud infirad) determines whether he must follow the imam in sujud tilawah; if confirmed, following invalidates his prayer according to the relied-upon view.

Effect of Imam's Qahqaha and Intentional Hadath on the Masbuq's Prayer
Ruling on the imam's qahqaha/hadath after final sitting affecting masbuq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling regarding the effect of the imam's loud laughter (qahqaha) or intentional hadath after the final sitting on the masbuq's prayer, and identify the intra-Hanafi difference with Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Imam's prayer-invalidating act after final sitting also invalidates the masbuq's corresponding part per Abu Hanifa.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in congregational prayer: when the imam, after the final sitting (julus akhir) sufficient for tashahhud, commits an act that invalidates prayer—either loud laughter (qahqaha) or intentional nullification of wudu (hadath 'amd). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, not only does the imam's prayer become invalid in that part, but the same part of the masbuq's (latecomer's) prayer is also invalidated. This has practical implications for the masbuq, who cannot build his missed rak'ahs upon that invalid portion. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ, holding that the masbuq's prayer remains unaffected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its timing
Determine what the imam does (qahqaha or intentional hadath) and when it occurs—after the final sitting for the duration of tashahhud. This timing is crucial because the imam's prayer is nearly complete.
The imam's prayer is not invalidated entirely; only the part containing the invalidating act is affected.
2
State the ruling for the imam
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the imam's qahqaha or intentional hadath after the final sitting invalidates the part of the prayer in which it occurred. This means the imam's prayer in that segment is fasid (corrupt).
Loud laughter (qahqaha) invalidates both wudu and prayer; smile does not.
3
Extend the ruling to the masbuq
The same invalidating effect applies to the analogous part of the masbuq's prayer. Since the masbuq is still following the imam, his prayer in that corresponding part is also invalidated.
The masbuq's prayer is not fully void; only the part concurrent with the imam's invalid act is affected.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the masbuq's prayer is not invalidated because the imam's prayer itself is not invalidated after the final sitting in their view. This is a legitimate scholarly difference within the Hanafi school.
The matn and hashiya present Imam Abu Hanifa's position as the relied-upon view in this context, but the difference is acknowledged.
5
Apply the consequence
If the masbuq's prayer part is invalidated, he cannot build his missed rak'ahs upon that part. He must repeat those missed rak'ahs separately after the imam completes the prayer, or the entire prayer may need to be re-evaluated.
The practical impact is on how the masbuq completes his prayer after the imam's taslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يفسدها (قهقهة أمام المسبوق) وإن لم يتعمدها (وحدثه العمد) الحاصل بغير القهقهة إذا وجدا (بعد الجلوس الأخير قدر التشهد عند الإمام بفساد الجزء الذي حصلت فيه ويفسد مثله من صلاة المسبوق فلا يمكن بناؤه الفائت عليه
(And) invalidates it (the prayer) the loud laughter (qahqaha) of the imam of the masbuq, even if not intentional, and his intentional hadath (event) other than laughter, if they occur after the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud according to Imam, by invalidating the part in which it occurred, and the like from the prayer of the masbuq is invalidated, so he cannot build his missed (rak'ahs) upon it.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific situation: when the imam engages in loud laughter (qahqaha) or intentional hadath (nullification of wudu) after the final sitting (julus akhir) for the duration of tashahhud, according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The hadith of the imam invalidates the part of the prayer in which it occurred, and similarly invalidates the corresponding part of the masbuq's prayer. As a result, the masbuq cannot build his missed rak'ahs upon that invalid part. The hashiya notes that this is according to Imam Abu Hanifa (عند الإمام); Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ, holding that the masbuq's prayer is not invalidated by the imam's actions after the final sitting because the imam's prayer itself is not invalidated in their view. The ruling is specific to the situation where the masbuq's independence has not been confirmed (i.e., he is still in the process of following). If the masbuq had already established independence, his prayer would not be affected.

Key Terms
قهقهة (qahqaha): Loud laughter that disrupts prayer; it invalidates wudu and the prayer according to Hanafis.
حدث عمد (hadath 'amd): Intentional nullification of wudu, e.g., by passing wind or touching private parts intentionally.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): The latecomer in congregation who misses one or more rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The masbuq's prayer is not affected because he is separate
B) The masbuq's prayer is invalidated in that part and he cannot build upon it
C) The masbuq must perform sajdah sahw
D) The masbuq's prayer becomes void entirely

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the imam's qahqaha or intentional hadath after the final sitting invalidates the masbuq's corresponding prayer part, preventing him from building missed rak'ahs upon it.

Invalidity of Prayer Due to Early Salam with Mistaken Assumption
Ruling on invalidity due to early salam with mistaken assumptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that saying salam after two rak'ahs invalidates the prayer in non-two-rak'ah prayers, and identify the specific mistaken assumptions that trigger this invalidity.

Core Idea
Salam after two rak'ahs invalidates a prayer unless the prayer is inherently two rak'ahs.

This lesson examines a specific invalidator of prayer: performing the salutation (salam) after only two rak'ahs in a prayer that normally has more than two, such as Maghrib (three rak'ahs) or the four-rak'ah prayers of a resident (Zuhr, Asr, Isha). The Hanafi jurists clarify that this invalidates the prayer if the person acted out of a mistaken belief — for example, thinking he is a traveler, or that the prayer is Jumu'ah or Tarawih. Understanding this ruling helps maintain the integrity of the prayer by recognising when a premature ending is excusable and when it renders the prayer void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying salam after two rak'ahs in prayers that are normally more than two. The ruling: it invalidates the prayer (makes it fasid).
2
Recognise the mistaken assumptions
The invalidity occurs only if the salam was done due to a mistaken belief: thinking one is a traveler, thinking it is Jumu'ah, thinking it is Tarawih while it is 'Isha, or being a new Muslim unaware of the rak'ah count.
3
Distinguish two-rak'ah prayers
The rule does not apply to two-rak'ah prayers (Fajr, traveler's prayer, Jumu'ah). In those, salam after two is correct and the prayer is valid.
4
Note the critical refinement
The commentator clarifies that 'other than the two-rak'ah' specifically includes Maghrib and the four-rak'ah prayers of the resident, and suggests adding 'and it is Zuhr' for consistency in the example of Friday assumption.
This shows the precision of Hanafi jurists in enumerating invalidators.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يفسدها السلام على رأس ركعتين في غير الثنائية المغرب، ورباعية المقيم (ظاناً أنه مسافر) وهو مقيم (أو) ظانا (أنها الجمعة أو ظانا (أنها التراويح وهي العشاء أو كان قريب عهد بالإسلام) قوله : (المغرب ورباعية المقيم بدل من غير الثنائية. قوله: (أو ظانا أنها الجمعة) المناسب أن يزيد وهي الظهر مثلاً ليساوي ما قبله وما بعده.
(And) invalidates it the salam at the end of two rak'ahs in other than the two-rak'ah prayer of Maghrib and the four-rak'ah prayer of the resident, (assuming he is a traveler) while he is a resident, (or) assuming it is Friday, or assuming it is Tarawih while it is 'Isha, or he is new to Islam. His saying: (Maghrib and the four-rak'ah of the resident) are a substitute for 'other than the two-rak'ah'. His saying: (Or assuming it is Friday) it is appropriate to add 'and it is Zuhr for example' to match what came before and after.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage lists an invalidator of prayer: saying salam (salutation to end prayer) after only two rak'ahs in prayers that are normally more than two, such as Maghrib (which is three) and the four-rak'ah prayers of a resident (Zuhr, Asr, Isha). The invalidity occurs if the person says salam out of a mistaken belief, such as thinking he is a traveler (who shortens prayers to two), or thinking the prayer is Jumu'ah (which is two), or thinking it is Tarawih (which is two? Actually Tarawih is many, but here it seems confusion), or if the person is new to Islam and does not know the number of rak'ahs. The hashiya notes that the phrase 'غير الثنائية' includes Maghrib and the four-rak'ah prayers, so 'المغرب ورباعية المقيم' is a substitute or clarification. The commentator also notes that in the case of assuming it is Friday, it would be appropriate to add 'while it is Zuhr' to parallel the other examples. This shows the precision of the fuqaha in enumerating invalidators.

Key Terms
الثنائية (al-thunaiyyah): Two-rak'ah prayers, such as Fajr, traveler's shortened prayers, or Jumu'ah.
قريب عهد بالإسلام (qarib 'ahd bi'l-Islam): A new Muslim who may not be fully aware of the details of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Saying salam after two rak'ahs in Maghrib thinking one is a traveler
C) Saying salam after four rak'ahs in Zuhr prayer
D) Saying salam after two rak'ahs in Jumu'ah

Key Takeaway
Saying salam after two rak'ahs invalidates any prayer that is inherently more than two rak'ahs, regardless of the worshipper's mistaken belief about the prayer's nature.

Invalidators of the Masbuq's Prayer and the Effect of the Imam's Actions
List of invalidators with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the masbuq's prayer becomes invalid and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the imam's laughter after the final sitting.

Core Idea
The masbuq's prayer is invalidated by specific actions before independence; the imam's post-final sitting laughter is disputed among Hanafi imams.

The latecomer (masbuq) has a unique status in congregational prayer: his prayer is partially dependent on the imam until he completes his own prayer. This lesson explores the specific invalidators for the masbuq, particularly when the imam's actions after the final sitting affect the masbuq's prayer. We will examine the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions on whether the imam's laughter invalidates the masbuq's prayer, and understand the relied-upon fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the masbuq's dependency period
The masbuq is connected to the imam until he becomes independent by standing to complete his missed rak'ahs. Invalidators must be assessed relative to this dependency.
2
List the invalidators specific to the masbuq
Walk through each invalidator mentioned in the text: standing before imam's tashahhud, not repeating final sitting after a sajdah, performing a rukn while sleeping, imam's laughter/hadath after final sitting, premature salam.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Focus on the ruling on the imam's laughter/hadath after the final sitting. Identify that Imam Abu Hanifa says the masbuq's prayer is invalid, while the Sahibayn say it remains valid.
4
Analyze the reasoning
Trace the dalil: Abu Hanifa argues that the imam's prayer becomes invalid in that part, so the masbuq's following part is also invalid. The Sahibayn argue that the imam's prayer is not invalidated because it is after the final sitting, so the masbuq's prayer remains valid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Note that the later scholars and the fatwa are with the Sahibayn. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: in practice, if the imam laughs after the final sitting, the masbuq's prayer is valid.

His prayer becomes invalid. We have restricted the standing of the masbuq to after the imam's sitting to the extent of the tashahhud because if it was before, it is not sufficient, as the imam still has an obligation upon him that the masbuq cannot perform alone, so his prayer becomes invalid. (And) it is invalidated by: (not repeating the final sitting after performing a sajdah of the prayer or a sajdah of recitation that one remembers after sitting) because the final sitting is not considered valid except after all the integral parts, since it is for sealing the prayer, and there is no conflict, and the final sitting is annulled by the sajdah of recitation according to the chosen view. (And) it is invalidated by: (not repeating an integral that he performed while sleeping) because the condition for its validity is performing it while awake. (And) it is invalidated by: (laughter of the imam in front of the masbuq) even if not intentional, and his intentional impurity other than laughter, if they occur after the final sitting to the extent of the tashahhud, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, invalidates the part in which it occurred, and similarly invalidates an equivalent part of the masbuq's prayer, so he cannot build upon the missed part. (And) it is invalidated by: (the salam at the end of two rak'ahs in other than the two-rak'ah prayer, the Maghrib, and the four-rak'ah of the resident, thinking he is a traveler while he is a resident, or thinking it is Friday, or thinking it is tarawih while it is 'Isha, or one who is a recent convert to Islam, or one who grew up Muslim ignorant such that he thought the obligatory prayer is two rak'ahs), in other than the two-rak'ah prayer, because it is an intentional salam with the intention of ending, before its time, so the prayer becomes invalid. Whoever does not restrict [the condition] and the imam performs a sajdah, it is obligatory to follow him, and what he performed is annulled; but if he continues his prayer, it is valid because following is obligatory as it is in an obligatory act, and leaving an obligatory act does not necessitate invalidity, and he performs sajdah al-sahw after completing it, by istihsan. If the masbuq follows his imam in sajdah al-sahw and it becomes clear that there is no sahw upon him, then the masbuq's prayer is valid according to the later scholars, and upon it is the fatwa. If the imam performs sajdah al-tilawah, then if the masbuq's independence is not established, he must return and what he performed before is not considered; if he does not return, his prayer is invalid because the sitting is annulled with respect to the imam, so it is annulled with respect to him. If his independence is established by tying the rak'ah to the sajdah, then if he returns, his prayer is invalid in one narration; if he does not return and continues, there are two narrations, and the apparent narration is invalidity, and it is the sounder of the two narrations, because returning to sajdah al-tilawah annuls the sitting, so it becomes clear that the masbuq became independent in a place where following was required, so his prayer is invalid. End from the Sharh, abridged. His statement: 'because it is for sealing it and therefore it is called final.' His statement: 'according to the chosen view' because it is an effect of recitation, so it takes its ruling, and it is the soundest; it is said it does not annul it because it is obligatory so it does not annul the obligatory, and Shams al-A'imma chose this, as stated by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'according to Imam' – and the two said: the masbuq's prayer is not invalidated by the imam's laughter after he sat to the extent of the tashahhud, because the imam's prayer is not invalidated by it. Or he restricted his statement to after the final sitting because if intentional impurity occurs before the sitting, everyone's prayer is invalidated by agreement. And he restricted the invalidation of the masbuq's prayer according to Imam to when his independence is not established. So if he stands before his salam leaving an obligatory act, then performs a rak'ah and performs sajdah for it, then the imam does that, his prayer is not invalidated because his independence is established. Al-Sayyid mentioned this, and it appears that the correction of the two companions' statement in the twelve issues applies to this part, so reflect. His statement: 'and it is invalidated by the salam' even if he did not say 'alaykum,' from al-Bahr, from al-Khulasah, mentioned by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'Maghrib and four-rak'ah of the resident' is a substitute for 'other than the two-rak'ah.' His statement: 'or thinking it is Friday' – it would be appropriate to add 'while it is Zuhr' to parallel what precedes and follows.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a detailed commentary on the invalidators of prayer (mufsidat) specific to the masbuq (one who joins the prayer late). The text first lists the invalidators, then provides a separate discussion on following the imam in sajdah, and finally gives explanatory notes on specific phrases. The key rulings are: (1) The masbuq's standing after the imam's sitting is valid only if after the imam's tashahhud; if before, the masbuq's prayer is invalid. (2) If the masbuq performs a sajdah (either for tilawah or a missed sajdah) after the final sitting, he must repeat the sitting; otherwise his prayer is invalid. (3) Performing a rukn while sleeping requires repetition. (4) The imam's laughter or intentional hadath after the masbuq's final sitting invalidates the masbuq's prayer according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it does not, as the imam's prayer itself is not invalidated. The relied-upon fatwa is according to the later scholars that the masbuq's prayer remains valid in such cases. (5) Saying salam prematurely (e.g., at two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer) out of ignorance or mistaken assumption invalidates the prayer. The passage then discusses the masbuq's following of the imam in sajdah al-sahw or tilawah: if the masbuq's independence is not established, he must follow, otherwise his prayer may be invalid. This is a complex area with multiple narrations. The commentary underscores the principle that the masbuq's prayer depends on the imam's until he becomes independent. This passage is essential for understanding the precise conditions under which a masbuq's prayer is valid or invalid.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): The latecomer who joins the congregation after the imam has started the prayer, missing one or more rak'ahs.
الجلوس الأخير (al-julus al-akhir): The final sitting in prayer for reciting the tashahhud, which seals the prayer.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): Prostration required when reciting certain verses of the Quran during prayer or outside it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling of the Sahibayn regarding the masbuq's prayer if the imam laughs after the final sitting?
A) The masbuq's prayer is invalid.
B) The masbuq's prayer remains valid.
C) The masbuq's prayer is valid only if he completes it separately.
D) The masbuq's prayer is invalid only if the imam intended to laugh.

Key Takeaway
The masbuq's prayer is invalidated by specific actions; the imam's laughter after the final sitting does not invalidate the masbuq's prayer according to the relied-upon fatwa.
