Recitation Errors and Their Effect on Prayer
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on recitation errors and the final fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for different types of recitation errors in prayer and apply the mufta bihi position to determine validity.

Core Idea
Grammatical errors in recitation do not invalidate prayer according to the fatwa, even if meaning changes.

Does a slip of the tongue during Qur'an recitation break your prayer? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer based on the type of error, the intention, and the imams' differences. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the principles and the relied-upon fatwa, which prioritises removing hardship for the common person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognise that the issue is about recitation errors in prayer. The ruling (valid or invalid) depends on the error type and whether it was intentional.
2
Understand the three imams' positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider whether the meaning changed grossly. Abu Yusuf distinguishes based on whether the mistaken wording exists in the Qur'an. Note that i'rab is not considered at all by Abu Yusuf.
3
Note the later consensus and fatwa
The later scholars (mutakhkhirin) agreed that errors in i'rab do not invalidate, even if they cause a change in meaning, due to widespread difficulty. The fatwa is given with Abu Yusuf's view.
4
Distinguish intentional vs unintentional
Intentional errors that grossly change meaning or imply disbelief invalidate the prayer. Unintentional errors or those that do not change meaning much are pardoned.
5
Apply to specific cases
Consider examples: lightening a shaddah (takhfif), shortening a madd, or reciting with incorrect case endings. Evaluate each using the principles above.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تكميل: زلة القارىء من أهم المسائل وهي مبنية على قواعد ناشئة من الاختلافات لا كما توهم أنه ليس لها قاعدة تبني عليها، فالأصل فيها عند الإمام، ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى تغير المعنى تغيراً فاحشاً وعدمه للفساد وعدمه مطلقاً سواء كان اللفظ موجوداً في القرآن، أو لم يكن وعند أبي يوسف رحمه الله إن كان اللفظ نظيره موجوداً في القرآن لا تفسد مطلقاً تغير المعنى تغيراً فاحشاً، أو لا وإن لم يكن موجوداً في القرآن تفسد مطلقاً، ولا يعتبر الإعراب أصلاً، ومحل الاختلاف في الخطأ والنسيان أما في العمد فتفسد به مطلقاً، بالاتفاق إذا كان مما يفسد الصلاة أما إذا كان ثناء فلا يفسد ولو تعمد ذلك أفاده ابن أمير حاج، وفي هذا الفصل مسائل. الأولى الخطأ في الإعراب، ويدخل فيه تخفيف المشدد، وعكسه وقصر الممدود، وعكسه، وفك المدغم ، وعكسه فإن لم يتغير به المعنى لا تفسد به صلاته بالإجماع، كما في المضمرات، وإذا تغير المعنى نحو أن يقرأ وإذ ابتلى ابراهيم ربه برفع ،ابراهيم، ونصب ربه فالصحيح عنهما الفساد، وعلى قياس قول أبي يوسف : لا تفسد لأنه لا يعتبر الإعراب، وبه يفتى وأجمع المتأخرون كمحمد بن مقاتل، ومحمد بن سلام واسمعيل الزاهد وأبي بكر سعيد البلخي، والهندواني وابن الفضل والحلواني على أن الخطأ في الإعراب لا يفسد مطلقاً، وإن كان مما اعتقاده كفر لأن أكثر الناس لا يميزون بين وجوه الإعراب، وفي اختيار الصواب في الإعراب، إيقاع الناس في الحرج، وهو مرفوع شرعاً، وعلى هذا مشى في الخلاصة، فقال: وفي النوازل لا تفسد في الكل وبه يفتى وينبغي ان يكون هذا فيما إذا كان خطأ أو غلطاً، وهو لا يعلم، أو تعمد ذلك ما لا يغير المعنى كثيراً كنصب الرحمن في قوله تعالى : الرحمن على العرش استوى أما لو تعمد مع ما يغير المعنى كثيراً، أو يكون اعتقاده كفراً فالفساد حينئذ أقل الأحوال، والمفتى به قول أبي يوسف، وأما تخفيف المشدد كما لو قرأ إياك نعبد أو رب العالمين بالتخفيف فقال المتأخرون لا تفسد مطلقاً، من غير استثناء على المختار لأن ترك المد والتشديد بمنزلة الخطأ في الإعراب كما في قاضيخان، وهو الأصح كما في المضمرات، وكذا نص في الذخيرة على أنه الأصح كما في ابن أمير حاج، وحكم تشديد المخفف كحكم
Completion: The slip of the reciter (zallat al-qari') is among the most important issues, and it is based on principles arising from differences, not as is mistakenly thought that it has no basis. The fundamental principle according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) is: a gross change in meaning and its absence, for invalidity and non-invalidity absolutely, whether the word exists in the Qur'an or not. According to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him): if the word's equivalent exists in the Qur'an, it does not invalidate absolutely, whether the meaning changes grossly or not; and if it does not exist in the Qur'an, it invalidates absolutely. Grammatical i'rab is not considered at all. The point of difference is in error and forgetfulness; as for intentional [mistake], it invalidates absolutely, by agreement, if it is something that invalidates the prayer. But if it is praise (thana'), it does not invalidate even if intentional, as Ibn Amir Hajj mentioned. In this chapter are issues. First: error in i'rab (grammatical inflection). This includes lightening of a shaddah and its opposite, shortening of a lengthened letter and its opposite, separating an idgham and its opposite. If the meaning does not change, the prayer is not invalidated by consensus, as in al-Mudmarat. If the meaning changes, such as reciting 'Wa idh ibtala Ibrahima Rabbahu' with the raf' of 'Ibrahima' and nasb of 'Rabbahu,' then the sound [view] from the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is invalidity. By analogy with the statement of Abu Yusuf: it does not invalidate because i'rab is not considered, and with this the fatwa is given. The later scholars such as Muhammad ibn Muqatil, Muhammad ibn Salam, Isma'il al-Zahid, Abu Bakr Sa'id al-Balkhi, al-Hinduwani, Ibn al-Fadl, and al-Halwani agreed that error in i'rab does not invalidate absolutely, even if it entails disbelief, because most people cannot distinguish between aspects of i'rab, and choosing correctness in i'rab causes hardship, which is removed by Shari'ah. Al-Khulasah followed this, stating: In al-Nawazil, it does not invalidate in all cases, and with this the fatwa is given. It is appropriate that this applies when it is a mistake or error, and he does not know, or he intentionally does that which does not change the meaning much, like placing nasb on al-Rahman in the verse 'al-Rahmanu 'ala al-'arshi istawa.' As for intentionally doing that which changes the meaning much or entails disbelief, then invalidity is [at least] the least of the states, and the mufta bihi is the statement of Abu Yusuf. Regarding lightening of a shaddah, such as reciting 'Iyyaka na'budu' or 'Rabb al-'alamin' with takhfif, the later scholars say it does not invalidate absolutely, without exception, according to the chosen view, because leaving tashdid is like error in i'rab, as in Qadikhan, and it is the soundest as in al-Mudmarat. Similarly, it is stated in al-Dhakhirah as the soundest, as in Ibn Amir Hajj. The ruling of tashdid of a lightened letter is like the ruling [of the opposite].
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi provides a comprehensive treatment of the effect of recitation errors on the validity of prayer, known as zallat al-qari'. It introduces the fundamental principles from the three major Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider whether the meaning changed grossly, while Abu Yusuf distinguishes based on whether the wording exists in the Qur'an. The later consensus among the mutakhkhirin is that grammatical errors (i'rab) do not invalidate the prayer, to avoid hardship, and the fatwa is given accordingly. However, intentional changes that grossly alter meaning or imply disbelief do invalidate. The passage then applies these principles to specific cases: lightening of shaddah, shortening of madd, etc. The relied-upon position for the fatwa is that of Abu Yusuf regarding i'rab, and the later scholars' view on takhfif of mushaddad is that it does not invalidate. This passage is crucial for understanding the Hanafi position on the validity of prayer when recitation errors occur.

Key Terms
زلة القارىء (zallat al-qari'): The slip or mistake of the reciter during prayer, specifically regarding recitation errors.
الإعراب (al-i'rab): Grammatical inflection, i.e., the case endings (raf', nasb, jarr) in Arabic that affect meaning.
تخفيف المشدد (takhfif al-mushaddad): Pronouncing a doubled consonant (shaddah) as a single consonant, i.e., without emphasis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid.
B) The prayer is valid.
C) The prayer is valid but sajdah al-sahw is required.
D) The prayer is invalid only if intentional.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa is that grammatical errors in recitation do not invalidate the prayer, reflecting the principle of removing hardship, while intentional gross changes may still invalidate.

Rulings on Recitation Mistakes (Zallat al-Qari) in Salah
Explains Hanafi rulings on recitation mistakes and the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for i‘rab, waqf/ibtida’, and letter substitution mistakes in salah, and explain why the later Hanafi fatwa is lenient.

Core Idea
Most recitation mistakes do not invalidate salah; hardship is removed.

Recitation mistakes during salah are common, especially among non-Arabic speakers. The Hanafi school addresses these with a nuanced approach: while early masters (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) invalidated salah if the meaning changed grossly, the later scholars (muta’akhkhirun) adopted a more lenient position based on necessity and the removal of hardship. This lesson unpacks the three main categories of mistakes and the final fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of recitation mistakes
The passage breaks mistakes into: (1) errors in i‘rab (inflection), including tashdid/madd, (2) errors in stopping and starting (waqf/ibtida’), and (3) substituting one letter for another. Note the ruling for each.
These categories are exhaustive in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Distinguish the early Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: gross change of meaning invalidates. Abu Yusuf: i‘rab is not considered at all; for substitution, if the said word exists in the Quran, no invalidation.
Abu Yusuf’s view is more lenient regarding i‘rab.
3
Identify the later scholars’ consensus
The later scholars (e.g., Ibn Muqatil, al-Halwani) ruled that i‘rab mistakes and most other errors do not invalidate absolutely, due to hardship (al-haraj marfu‘).
This is the fatwa used today in the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the ruling to specific examples
Use examples from the passage: reciting 'Ibrahima Rabbahu' with wrong i‘rab, or 'al-sirata alladhina' with added article. Determine validity based on the mufta bihi view.
Intentional mistakes that change meaning grossly may still invalidate.
5
Understand the basis of istihsan
The leniency is based on istihsan (juristic preference) and the principle that hardship is removed. The illa (effective cause) is prevalence of need (umum al-balwa).
This protects the common person without requiring perfect tajweed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( لأنه سلام عمد على جهة القطع) أي بخلاف ما إذا سلم على رأس الركعتين من الرباعية على ظن أنها الرابعة حيث لا تفسد ذكره السيد، وبقي من المفسدات بالقلب، وكل ما أوجب الوضوء، والغسل وترك الركن بلا قضاء والشرط بلا عذر كذا في النهر .

تكميل: زلة القارىء من أهم المسائل وهي مبنية على قواعد ناشئة من الاختلافات لا كما توهم أنه ليس لها قاعدة تبني عليها، فالأصل فيها عند الإمام، ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى تغير المعنى تغيراً فاحشاً وعدمه للفساد وعدمه مطلقاً سواء كان اللفظ موجوداً في القرآن، أو لم يكن وعند أبي يوسف رحمه الله إن كان اللفظ نظيره موجوداً في القرآن لا تفسد مطلقاً تغير المعنى تغيراً فاحشاً، أو لا وإن لم يكن موجوداً في القرآن تفسد مطلقاً، ولا يعتبر الإعراب أصلاً، ومحل الاختلاف في الخطأ والنسيان أما في العمد فتفسد به مطلقاً، بالاتفاق إذا كان مما يفسد الصلاة أما إذا كان ثناء فلا يفسد ولو تعمد ذلك أفاده ابن أمير حاج، وفي هذا الفصل مسائل.

المسألة الأولى الخطأ في الإعراب، ويدخل فيه تخفيف المشدد، وعكسه وقصر الممدود، وعكسه، وفك المدغم ، وعكسه فإن لم يتغير به المعنى لا تفسد به صلاته بالإجماع، كما في المضمرات، وإذا تغير المعنى نحو أن يقرأ وإذ ابتلى ابراهيم ربه برفع ،ابراهيم، ونصب ربه فالصحيح عنهما الفساد، وعلى قياس قول أبي يوسف : لا تفسد لأنه لا يعتبر الإعراب، وبه يفتى وأجمع المتأخرون كمحمد بن مقاتل، ومحمد بن سلام واسمعيل الزاهد وأبي بكر سعيد البلخي، والهندواني وابن الفضل والحلواني على أن الخطأ في الإعراب لا يفسد مطلقاً، وإن كان مما اعتقاده كفر لأن أكثر الناس لا يميزون بين وجوه الإعراب، وفي اختيار الصواب في الإعراب، إيقاع الناس في الحرج، وهو مرفوع شرعاً، وعلى هذا مشى في الخلاصة، فقال: وفي النوازل لا تفسد في الكل وبه يفتى وينبغي ان يكون هذا فيما إذا كان خطأ أو غلطاً، وهو لا يعلم، أو تعمد ذلك ما لا يغير المعنى كثيراً كنصب الرحمن في قوله تعالى : الرحمن على العرش استوى أما لو تعمد مع ما يغير المعنى كثيراً، أو يكون اعتقاده كفراً فالفساد حينئذ أقل الأحوال، والمفتى به قول أبي يوسف، وأما تخفيف المشدد كما لو قرأ إياك نعبد أو رب العالمين بالتخفيف فقال المتأخرون لا تفسد مطلقاً، من غير استثناء على المختار لأن ترك المد والتشديد بمنزلة الخطأ في الإعراب كما في قاضيخان، وهو الأصح كما في المضمرات، وكذا نص في الذخيرة على أنه الأصح كما في ابن أمير حاج، وحكم تشديد المخفف كحكم (1) قوله الارتداد بالقلب في نسخة زيادة والجنون والإغماء أهـ.

المسألة الثانية في الوقف والإبتداء في غيره وضعهما فإن لم يتغير به المعنى لا تفسد بالإجماع من المتقدمين والمتأخرين وإن تغير به المعنى فهي إختلاف، والفتوى على عدم الفساد بكل حال، وهو قول عامة علمائنا المتأخرين لأن في مراعاة الوقف، والوصل إيقاع الناس في الحرج لا سيما العوام والحرج مرفوع كما في الذخيرة والسراجية والنصاب، وفيه أيضاً لو ترك الوقف في جميع القرآن لا تفسد صلاته عندنا، وأما الحكم في قطع بعض الكلمة كما لو أراد أن يقول الحمد لله ، فقال : ال : فوقف على اللام أو على الحاء، أو على الميم، أو أراد أن يقرأ والعاديات فقال : والعا فوقف على العين لانقطاع نفسه أو نسيان الباقي، ثم تمم، أو انتقل إلى آية أخرى فالذي عليه عامة المشايخ عدم الفساد مطلقاً وان غير المعنى للضرورة، وعموم البلوى كما في الذخيرة، وهو الأصح كما ذكره أبو الليث.

المسألة الثالثة وضع حرف موضع حرف آخر فإن كانت الكلمة لا تخرج عن لفظ القرآن، ولم يتغير به المعنى المراد لا تفسد كما لو قرأ أن الظالمون بواو الرفع أو قال والأرض، وما دحاها مكان طحاها، وإن خرجت به عن لفظ القرآن ولم يتغير به المعنى لا تفسد عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف كما لو قرأ قيامين بالقسط مكان قوامين أو دواراً مكان دياراً وإن لم تخرج به عن لفظ القرآن، وتغير به المعنى فالخلاف بالعكس كما لو قرأ، وأنتم حامدون مكان سامدون وللمتأخرين قواعد آخر غير ما ذكرنا، واقتصرنا على ما سبق لإطرادها في كل الفروع بخلاف قواعد المتأخرين. واعلم أنه لا يقيس مسائل زلة القارىء بعضها على بعض إلا من له دراية باللغة والعربية والمعاني وغير ذلك مما يحتاج إليه التفسير كما في منية المصلي، وفي النهر وأحسن من لخص من كلامهم في زلة القارىء الكمال في زاد الفقيه فقال : إن كان الخطأ. الإعراب، ولم يتغير به المعنى ككسر قواماً مكان فتحها وفتح باء نعبد مكان ضمها لا تفسد، وإن غير كنصب همزة العلماء، وضم هاء الجلالة من قوله تعالى: (إنما يخشى الله العلماء [فاطر: ٣٥] تفسد على قول المتقدمين واختلف المتأخرون فقال ابن الفضل وابن مقاتل وأبو جعفر والحلواني وابن سلام واسمعيل الزاهدي لا تفسد وقول هؤلاء أوسع، وإن كان بوضع حرف مكان ،حرف، ولم يتغير المعنى نحو أياب مكان أواب لا تفسد، وعن أبي سعيد تفسد، وكثيراً ما يقع في قراءة بعض القرويين والأتراك والسودان، وياك نعبد بواو مكان الهمزة والصراط الذين بزيادة الألف واللام وصرحوا في الصورتين بعدم الفساد، وإن غير المعنى، وتمامه فيه، فليراجع والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
His statement: 'because it is intentional salutation with the intention of cutting off' i.e., contrary to when one gives salutation at the end of two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer thinking it is the fourth, where it does not invalidate. Thus in al-Nahr. Completion: The reciter's slip is among the most important issues, and it is built upon rules arising from differences, not as one might suppose that it has no rule to build upon. The principle according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them both) is gross change of meaning and its absence for invalidation and its absence absolutely, whether the word exists in the Quran or not. According to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), if a similar word exists in the Quran, it does not invalidate absolutely, whether the meaning changes grossly or not; and if a similar word does not exist in the Quran, it invalidates absolutely. And i'rab is not considered at all. The point of difference is in error and forgetfulness. As for intentional, it invalidates absolutely by consensus if it is something that invalidates prayer, but if it is praise, it does not invalidate even if intentional. This was conveyed by Ibn Amir Haj. In this chapter are issues. The first issue: error in i'rab, and included in it is lightening a doubled letter and its opposite, shortening a long letter and its opposite, separating an assimilated letter and its opposite. If the meaning does not change, the prayer is not invalidated by consensus, as in al-Mudmarat. If the meaning changes, like reciting 'Wa idh ibtala Ibrahima Rabbahu' with raf' on Ibrahim and nasb on Rabbahu, the correct [position] from them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is invalidation. On the analogy of Abu Yusuf's statement: it does not invalidate because i'rab is not considered, and according to this fatwa is given. The later scholars such as Muhammad b. Muqatil, Muhammad b. Salam, Isma'il al-Zahid, Abu Bakr Sa'id al-Balkhi, al-Hindawani, Ibn al-Fadl, and al-Halwani agreed that error in i'rab does not invalidate absolutely, even if its belief is disbelief, because most people cannot distinguish between aspects of i'rab. And in choosing correctness in i'rab, there is placing people in hardship, and hardship is removed by shari'ah. Upon this al-Khulasa proceeded, saying: In al-Nawazil, it does not invalidate in all cases, and according to this fatwa is given. This should be when it is an error or mistake and he does not know, or if he intentionally does that which does not change the meaning much, like nasb of al-Rahman in His statement: 'al-Rahman 'ala al-'arsh istawa'. But if he intentionally does what changes the meaning much, or its belief is disbelief, then invalidation is [the ruling] in the least of cases. The mufta bihi is the statement of Abu Yusuf. As for lightening a doubled letter, like reciting 'Iyyaka na'budu' or 'Rabb al-'alamin' with lightening, the later scholars said it does not invalidate absolutely, without exception, according to the chosen view, because leaving madd and tashdid is like error in i'rab, as in Qadikhan, and it is the most correct as in al-Mudmarat. Similarly, it is stated in al-Dhakhira that it is the most correct, as in Ibn Amir Haj. The ruling on doubling a lightened letter is like its opposite in terms of difference and detail. Similarly, pronouncing an assimilated letter clearly and its opposite: all are one type as in al-Halabi. The second issue: regarding stopping and starting (waqf wa ibtida') in other than its place. If the meaning does not change, it does not invalidate by consensus of the early and later scholars. If the meaning changes, there is difference, and the fatwa is on non-invalidation in any case, which is the statement of the generality of our later scholars, because observing stopping and starting places people in hardship, especially the common folk, and hardship is removed, as in al-Dhakhira, al-Sirajiyyah, and al-Nisab. It also includes that if one leaves stopping throughout the entire Qur'an, his prayer does not invalidate according to us. As for the ruling on cutting part of a word, like if he wants to say 'al-hamdu lillahi' and says 'al', stopping on the lam or on the ha, or on the mim; or if he wants to recite 'wa al-'adiyat' and says 'wa al-'a', stopping on the 'ayn due to breathlessness or forgetting the rest, then completes it, or moves to another verse, the view of the generality of scholars is non-invalidation absolutely, even if it changes the meaning, due to necessity and widespread need, as in al-Dhakhira, and it is the most correct as mentioned by Abu al-Layth. The third issue: placing one letter in place of another. If the word does not leave the wording of the Quran, and the intended meaning does not change, it does not invalidate, as if he recites 'anna al-zalimina' with the waw of raf', or says 'wa al-ard, wa ma daha' instead of 'tahaha'. If it leaves the wording of the Quran but the meaning does not change, it does not invalidate according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf, as if he recites 'qiyyamin bi al-qist' instead of 'qawwamin' or 'diwaran' instead of 'diyaran'. If it does not leave the wording of the Quran but the meaning changes, the difference is the opposite, as if he recites 'wa antum hamidun' instead of 'samidun'. The later scholars have other rules besides what we mentioned, and we restricted ourselves to the above because they apply uniformly to all branches, unlike the rules of the later scholars. Know that one should not analogize some issues of the reciter's slip to others except one who has knowledge of language, grammar, meanings, and other things needed for interpretation, as in Munyat al-Musalli. In al-Nahr: The best summary of their statements on the reciter's slip is that of al-Kamal in Zad al-Faqih: If the error is in i'rab and the meaning does not change, like kasr of 'qawaman' instead of its fat'ha, and fat'h of the ba of 'na'budu' instead of its dammah, it does not invalidate. If it changes, like nasb of the hamza of 'al-'ulama' and damm of the ha of al-jalal in His statement 'innama yakhsha Allahu min 'ibadihi al-'ulama' [Fatir: 35], it invalidates according to the early scholars, and the later scholars differed: Ibn al-Fadl, Ibn Muqatil, Abu Ja'far, al-Halwani, Ibn Salam, and Isma'il al-Zahidi said it does not invalidate, and their statement is more expansive. If it is putting one letter in place of another and the meaning does not change, like 'ayyab' instead of 'awwab', it does not invalidate, and from Abu Sa'id [it is reported] it invalidates. Frequently this occurs in the recitation of some villagers, Turks, and Sudanese: 'wa yaka na'budu' with waw instead of hamza, and 'al-sirata alladhina' with addition of alif and lam, and they explicitly state in both forms non-invalidation, even if the meaning changes. The rest is in it (Zad al-Faqih), so refer to it. And Allah most high knows best, and I ask forgiveness from Allah the Almighty.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi treatment of the rulings on recitation mistakes (zallat al-qari) during salah. It begins by noting that this topic is of great importance and is based on rules arising from differences among the early Hanafi masters. The author explains the foundational principle: According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, a mistake invalidates the prayer if it grossly changes the meaning, regardless of whether the word is from the Quran or not. According to Abu Yusuf, if the mistake results in a word that exists in the Quran (even if different meaning), it does not invalidate; otherwise it does. However, i'rab (grammatical inflection) is not considered at all in Abu Yusuf's view, and the fatwa is given on his position. The later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) went further, ruling that errors in i'rab do not invalidate the prayer absolutely, due to the widespread difficulty and the principle of removing hardship (al-haraj marfu'). This is the mufta bihi position. The passage then addresses three specific issues: (1) errors in i'rab, including related matters like tashdid/madd etc.; (2) stopping and starting incorrectly; (3) substituting one letter for another. For each, the author explains the ruling based on the early and later positions, with the predominant view being non-invalidation unless there is a gross change of meaning in the specific case. The commentary emphasizes that the later scholars' positions are more accommodating to avoid hardship for the common people. The passage also includes a quote from al-Kamal in Zad al-Faqih summarizing the rulings. Overall, the Hanafi school adopts a flexible approach to recitation mistakes, prioritizing the validity of the prayer and the principle of removing hardship over strict grammatical or phonetic accuracy.

Key Terms
زلة القارئ (zallat al-qari): Mistake or slip made by the reciter during Quran recitation in prayer, including errors in pronunciation, inflection, stopping, or substitution of letters.
الإعراب (al-i'rab): Grammatical inflection (case endings) of words, including vowel endings indicating nominative, accusative, genitive, etc.
الحرج (al-haraj): Hardship or difficulty; the principle that shari'ah does not impose obligations that cause undue hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a person who mistakenly recites 'Ibrahima' with raf' instead of nasb in Surah al-Baqarah during salah?
A) The prayer is invalid because the meaning changes.
B) The prayer is valid and no compensation is required.
C) The prayer is valid but requires sajdah al-sahw.
D) The prayer is invalid only if done intentionally.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, especially the later scholars, rules that most recitation mistakes in salah do not invalidate the prayer, based on the principle of removing hardship.

Rulings on Recitation Errors in Prayer: Hardship and Umum al-Balwa
Detailed rulings on recitation errors and their effect on prayer validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation errors that change meaning, apply the principles of raf' al-haraj and umum al-balwa, and distinguish between the positions of earlier and later Hanafi scholars.

Core Idea
Most recitation errors do not invalidate prayer—the principle of removing hardship overrides strict recitation rules.

Many worshippers worry that a mistake in Quran recitation during prayer might nullify their salah. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: with few exceptions, even significant errors do not invalidate the prayer. The school's later scholars relied on the principles of hardship (haraj) and widespread occurrence (umum al-balwa) to bring ease to the common person. We will explore three types of errors, the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and the evidence for the lenient view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three error types
The passage covers three categories: (1) stopping and starting (waqf/ibtida') out of place; (2) cutting a word mid-stream (e.g., stopping on a single letter); (3) substituting one letter for another. For each, note whether meaning changes.
These are the main scenarios of 'zillat al-qari'.
2
Note the consensus on no-invalidation when meaning unchanged
The text states that if the error does not change the meaning, there is consensus (ijma') that the prayer is valid. This applies to all three types.
This is the baseline ruling.
3
Understand the disagreement when meaning changes
When meaning changes, earlier scholars (mutqaddimun) held that prayer is invalid, but later scholars (mutakhkhirun) ruled it remains valid due to hardship. The fatwa follows the later view.
The shift from strict to lenient is based on raf' al-haraj.
4
Apply the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on letter substitution
In the third issue (letter substitution that departs from Quranic wording but meaning unchanged), Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say valid, Abu Yusuf says invalid. The mufta bihi is the view of the two.
This shows how even within the school, ease is preferred.

كما لو قرأ، وأنتم حامدون مكان سامدون وللمتأخرين قواعد آخر غير ما ذكرنا، واقتصرنا على ما سبق لإطرادها في كل الفروع بخلاف قواعد المتأخرين. واعلم أنه لا يقيس مسائل زلة القارىء بعضها على بعض إلا من له Commentary
This passage is a detailed treatment of rulings on recitation errors (zillat al-qari) in prayer, extracted from the super-commentary of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah. The author first clarifies that the earlier discussion (possibly on mudgham) treats all types as one category. Then he presents the second issue: stopping and starting (al-waqf wa al-ibtida') in recitation. The consensus of earlier and later scholars is that if stopping does not change the meaning, it does not invalidate prayer. If it changes the meaning, there is disagreement; however, the fatwa is on non-invalidation in all cases, based on the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj), especially for common people. This is supported by citations from al-Dhakhira, al-Sirajiyya, and al-Nisab. Even completely abandoning proper stopping throughout the Quran does not invalidate prayer according to the Hanafi school. The ruling on cutting a word mid-stream (e.g., stopping on a single letter due to breathlessness) is also non-invalidating absolutely, according to the majority of scholars, including Abu al-Layth. The third issue concerns substituting one letter for another. If the word remains Quranic and the meaning unchanged, prayer is valid. If the word becomes non-Quranic but meaning unchanged, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it is valid, while Abu Yusuf says it invalidates. If the word remains Quranic but meaning changes, the disagreement is reversed. The author then notes that later scholars have different principles, but these are not covered. He emphasizes that analogizing zillat al-qari cases requires deep linguistic and exegetical knowledge, citing Munyat al-Musalli. Finally, he presents al-Kamal's summary from Zad al-Faqih, categorizing errors by type: i'rab errors that do not change meaning are non-invalidating; those that change meaning invalidate according to earlier scholars, but later scholars like Ibn al-Fadl, Ibn Muqatil, and others say they do not. Similarly, letter substitution without meaning change is non-invalidating, though Abu Sa'id disagreed. Common errors like pronouncing 'iyyaka' with waw or adding 'al' to 'sirat' are explicitly ruled non-invalidating even if meaning changes. The passage concludes by referring to the full discussion elsewhere.

Key Terms
الوقف والإبتداء (al-waqf wa al-ibtida'): Stopping and starting in Quran recitation; here specifically about where one pauses and resumes.
زلة القارئ (zillat al-qari): Mistake made by the reciter in prayer, including errors in pronunciation, grammar, or stopping.
الحرج (al-haraj): Hardship; a legal cause for leniency in rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Hanafi school prioritizes ease: most recitation errors do not invalidate prayer, especially when due to widespread difficulty.

Looking at a Written Text During Prayer: Valid but Disliked
Ruling on looking at text during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on looking at a written text during prayer and explain why it does not invalidate, distinguishing between intentional and unintentional looking.

Core Idea
Looking and understanding without speech does not invalidate prayer.

Is it permissible to glance at a book or phone during prayer? The Hanafi school clarifies that the act of looking and understanding does not constitute speech, which is the key element that would break prayer. However, intentional looking is considered a breach of adab (etiquette). This lesson unpacks the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is looking at a written text and understanding it during prayer.
This includes Quran or any other text.
2
Determine the ruling
The prayer is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh tanzih) if intentional.
If unintentional, it is not disliked.
3
Understand the legal reason
Invalidation requires actual speech (nutaq); looking and mental comprehension do not qualify.
The author says 'li-‘adam al-nutaq'.
4
Note the exception
If the look is unintentional and understanding occurs, it is not disliked.
The commentary specifies 'bi al-qasd'.
5
Relate to khushu'
Abandoning khushu' affects perfection, not validity.
Khushu' is sunnah, not fard.

Source Text

قصده، وفهمه فلا يكره. قوله : (أو أكل ما بين أسنانه قيد به لأنه لو تناول شيئاً من خارج، ولو سمسمة، أو قطرة مطر فوصلت إلى حلقه فسدت صلاته، وصومه إذا كان ذاكراً. قوله : (وكان دون الحمصة أما إذا كان قدر الحمصة فأكثر أفسدها كما يفسد الصوم فما يفسدها يفسده وما لا فلا. قوله : (بلا عمل كثير أما إذا كان مضغه كثيراً فلا خلاف في الفساد كما في البحر بخلاف إبتلاع القليل بعمل قليل لأنه تبع لريقه، ولا يمكن الاحتراز عنه قوله: (کره) هو في المسجد، والذي يقتضيه النظر الفقهي عدم التعرض له إلى أن يفرغ من صلاته فيلقيه في محل مباح ولا يأكله فقد ورد كلوا الوغم وأطرحوا الفغم. قال ابن الأثير في نهايته: الوغم، ما يتساقط من الطعام والفم ما يخرجه الخلال من بين الأسنان اهـ أي ارموا ما يخرجه الخلال، وكذا ما يخرج بنفسه خصوصاً ان مكث كثيراً لتغيره وإن أكله مع ذلك كره خارجها أيضاً. قوله : (أو مز ما عبر بهذا التركيب لصحته لوقوعه في أفصح كلام قال تعالى: سأل سائل) . قوله : (سواء المرأة والكلب أشار به إلى خلاف الظاهرية، فقالوا إن مرورها بين يديه، وكذا الكلب والحمار مفسد قوله : ( لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم الخ ) ولما أخرج أبو داود عن الفضل بن عباس أنانا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ونحن في بادية لنا ومعه عباس فصلى في صحراء ليس بين يديه سترة، وكلبة وحمارة يعبثان بين يديه فما بالي بذلك قوله: (فإنما هو شيطان) سواء كان آدمياً، أو غيره لأن الشيطان . قال تعالى: شياطين الإنس والجن) [الأنعام: ٦] . يعم
Chapter on what does not invalidate prayer: (If the praying person looks at a written text and understands it, whether it is Quran or something else, intending to understand or not, he does bad etiquette, and his prayer does not invalidate due to not uttering speech; or eats what is between his teeth and it is less than a chickpea without much action) it is disliked and does not invalidate due to difficulty of avoiding it. If he swallows what melted of sugar in his mouth, it invalidates; if he swallowed it before prayer and finds its sweetness during prayer, it does not invalidate. Or [a passerby?] passes in his prostration place, it does not invalidate, whether a woman, dog, or donkey, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Nothing cuts the prayer; repel as much as you can, for it is a devil.' And the responsible passerby sins if deliberate, due to his saying: 'If the passerby knew what is between...' He said: (If the praying person looks at a written text, etc.) The reason for non-invalidation is that invalidation only occurs by recitation, and by looking and understanding, it has not occurred; the author indicated that by his saying 'due to not uttering.' He said: (Intended to understand) from this it is known that abandoning khushu' does not impair validity, but perfection. Therefore it is said in al-Khaniyya and al-Khulasa: If he reflects in prayer and remembers poetry or a sermon and recites it in his heart without speaking with his tongue, his prayer does not invalidate, as in al-Bahr. He said: (He does bad etiquette) because it is preoccupation from prayer; apparently the dislike is tanzihi, and this is only if intentional; if his sight falls upon it unintentionally and he understands, it is not disliked. He said: (Or eats what is between his teeth) he qualified it because if he takes something from outside, even a sesame seed or a raindrop reaching his throat, his prayer and fast invalidate if he is mindful. He said: (And it is less than a chickpea) but if it is the size of a chickpea or more, it invalidates as it invalidates the fast; what invalidates one invalidates the other, and what does not, does not. He said: (Without much action) but if his chewing is much, there is no disagreement on invalidation as in al-Bahr, unlike swallowing a little with little action because it is a follow-up of his saliva and cannot be avoided. He said: (It is disliked) i.e., in the mosque; and what legal reasoning requires is not to touch it until he finishes his prayer, then throw it in a permissible place and not eat it, for it has been narrated: 'Eat the crumbs and throw away the particles.' Ibn al-Athir said in his Nihaya: Al-wagham is what falls from food, and al-fugham is what the toothpick extracts from between the teeth; i.e., throw away what the toothpick extracts, and likewise what comes out by itself, especially if it stays long enough to change; and if he eats it, it is disliked even outside prayer. He said: (Or suck) he expressed it in this construction for its correctness because it occurs in the most eloquent speech, Allah said: 'Sa'ala sa'ilun.' He said: (Whether woman and dog) he indicated thereby opposition to the Zahiris, who said that her passage in front of him, and likewise dog and donkey, invalidates. He said: (Due to his saying, peace be upon him, etc.) And when Abu Dawud reported from al-Fadl ibn al-Abbas that the Messenger of Allah came to us while we were in our desert and with him was al-Abbas, and he prayed in an open plain with no screen in front of him, and a female dog and donkey were playing in front of him, so what is it to me? He said: (For it is a devil) whether human or otherwise, because the devil generalizes; Allah said: 'Shayatin of humans and jinn' [al-An'am 6:112].
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter 'What Does Not Invalidate Prayer' from Maraqi al-Falah. The matn lists several actions that do not break prayer, and the hashya explains each. First, looking at a written text (whether Quran or otherwise) and understanding it does not invalidate prayer because invalidation requires actual speech (nutaq). The commentator stresses that this is only if the looking is intentional; if unintentional, it is not even disliked. Lack of khushu' is a deficiency in perfection, not validity. Second, eating food particles left between the teeth that are less than a chickpea in size and not requiring much action is disliked but does not invalidate. The reason is the difficulty of avoidance. However, swallowing something from outside the mouth (like a sesame seed or raindrop) invalidates prayer and fast if done knowingly. If the particle is a chickpea-size or more, it invalidates. Much chewing invalidates by consensus. The preferred legal view is to spit out such particles after prayer rather than eat them. Third, sucking (mazz) something is not explicitly in the matn but the commentator clarifies it can be validly expressed. Fourth, the passage of a woman, dog, or donkey in front of the worshipper's prostration place does not invalidate prayer. The hadith 'Nothing cuts the prayer' and the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) are cited as proofs. The Zahiri school's contrary view is noted. The passage concludes that the passing being a devil does not affect validity.

Key Terms
الخشوع (al-khushu'): Humility and attentiveness in prayer; its lack does not invalidate but reduces reward.
الحمصة (al-himmisa): A chickpea; used as a measure for the size of food particles that if swallowed may affect validity.
الشيطان (al-shaytan): Devil; here applied to the passing being (woman, dog, donkey) as a metaphorical description, not literal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on intentionally looking at a written text during prayer without moving the lips?
A) Prayer is invalid.
B) Prayer is valid but disliked (makruh tanzih).
C) Prayer is valid and not disliked because it is not speech.
D) Prayer is valid only if the text is not Quran.

Key Takeaway
Looking at a text during prayer does not invalidate it; only verbal utterance breaks the prayer.

Eating Small Food Remnants During Prayer: The Chickpea Threshold
Rulings on eating particles during prayer with size and source conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on eating particles during prayer, including the chickpea threshold and the distinction between particles from inside and outside the mouth.

Core Idea
A food particle smaller than a chickpea ingested without much action does not invalidate prayer, but larger or externally sourced particles do.

What if a praying person swallows a small piece of food stuck between his teeth? The Hanafi school carefully differentiates based on size and source. A particle less than a chickpea and requiring minimal movement is overlooked due to difficulty of avoidance, but larger particles or anything swallowed from outside the mouth invalidates the prayer. This lesson clarifies the exact conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is eating remnants from between the teeth (remnants) vs. eating from outside the mouth.
Remnants are particles already in the mouth before prayer.
2
Determine the ruling
Valid if remnant is less than a chickpea and without much chewing; otherwise invalid.
Disliked (makruh tanzih) if valid, but invalid if conditions violated.
3
Understand the measure
The threshold is a chickpea (himmisa). If size equals or exceeds, prayer invalidates.
Same measure used for fasting.
4
Note the condition of action
Excessive chewing (much action) invalidates by consensus.
Swallowing with little action is tolerated.
5
Apply to related cases
If particle is from outside (even tiny) or if size is chickpea or more, invalidates.
External particles: e.g., a raindrop or sesame seed.

ولا تفسد لعسر الاحتراز عنه، وإذا ابتلع ما ذاب من سكر في فمه فسدت ولو ابتلعه قبل الصلاة ووجد حلاوته فيها لا تفسد أو [؟] مار في موضع سجوده لا تفسد) سواء المرأة والكلب والحمار لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : During prayer, you swallow a food particle that was between your teeth. Which condition would make your prayer valid (sahih) despite the act?
A) The particle was from outside the mouth.

C) The particle was the size of a chickpea or larger.

Passing in Front of a Praying Person: Woman, Dog, Donkey Do Not Invalidate
Ruling on the effect of passersby (woman, dog, donkey) during prayer with proof and dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that the passage of a woman, dog, or donkey in front of a praying person does not invalidate prayer, citing the hadith and rebutting the Zahiri argument.

Core Idea
Nothing cuts the prayer; the passerby sins if deliberate, but the prayer remains valid.

A widespread belief holds that if a woman, dog, or donkey passes in front of a praying person, the prayer is broken. The Hanafi school, based on explicit hadith and prophetic practice, firmly states that such passing does not invalidate prayer. This lesson examines the proof and the dispute with the Zahiri school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
Does the passing of a woman, dog, or donkey in front of a praying person invalidate the prayer?
This is a point of dispute between Hanafis and Zahiris.
2
State the Hanafi position
It does not invalidate prayer.
The prayer remains valid (sahih).
3
Cite the primary dalil
Hadith: 'لا يقطع الصلاة شيء' (Nothing cuts the prayer) and the Prophet's practice with a dog and donkey.
The hadith is explicit and supported by action.
4
Recognize the opposing view
Zahiri school holds that such passing invalidates prayer based on other hadith.
Commentary notes this as 'خلاف الظاهرية'.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Zahiri hadith are abrogated or refer to the screen (sutra); the reliable hadith show tolerance.
The Prophet prayed without a screen with a dog and donkey playing.
6
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafis do not require repetition; Zahiris would require repetition.
Practical consequence in daily prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الاحتراز عنه قوله: (کره) هو في المسجد، والذي يقتضيه النظر الفقهي عدم التعرض له إلى أن يفرغ من صلاته فيلقيه في محل مباح ولا يأكله فقد ورد كلوا الوغم وأطرحوا الفغم. قال ابن الأثير في نهايته: الوغم، ما يتساقط من الطعام والفم ما يخرجه الخلال من بين الأسنان اهـ أي ارموا ما يخرجه الخلال، وكذا ما يخرج بنفسه خصوصاً ان مكث كثيراً لتغيره وإن أكله مع ذلك كره خارجها أيضاً. قوله : (أو مز ما عبر بهذا التركيب لصحته لوقوعه في أفصح كلام قال تعالى: سأل سائل) . قوله : (سواء المرأة والكلب أشار به إلى خلاف الظاهرية، فقالوا إن مرورها بين يديه، وكذا الكلب والحمار مفسد قوله : ( لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم الخ ) ولما أخرج أبو داود عن الفضل بن عباس أنانا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ونحن في بادية لنا ومعه عباس فصلى في صحراء ليس بين يديه سترة، وكلبة وحمارة يعبثان بين يديه فما بالي بذلك قوله: (فإنما هو شيطان) سواء كان آدمياً، أو غيره لأن الشيطان . قال تعالى: شياطين الإنس والجن) [الأنعام: ٦] . يعم
Chapter on what does not invalidate prayer: (If the praying person looks at a written text and understands it, whether it is Quran or something else, intending to understand or not, he does bad etiquette, and his prayer does not invalidate due to not uttering speech; or eats what is between his teeth and it is less than a chickpea without much action) it is disliked and does not invalidate due to difficulty of avoiding it. If he swallows what melted of sugar in his mouth, it invalidates; if he swallowed it before prayer and finds its sweetness during prayer, it does not invalidate. Or [a passerby?] passes in his prostration place, it does not invalidate, whether a woman, dog, or donkey, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Nothing cuts the prayer; repel as much as you can, for it is a devil.' And the responsible passerby sins if deliberate, due to his saying: 'If the passerby knew what is between...' He said: (If the praying person looks at a written text, etc.) The reason for non-invalidation is that invalidation only occurs by recitation, and by looking and understanding, it has not occurred; the author indicated that by his saying 'due to not uttering.' He said: (Intended to understand) from this it is known that abandoning khushu' does not impair validity, but perfection. Therefore it is said in al-Khaniyya and al-Khulasa: If he reflects in prayer and remembers poetry or a sermon and recites it in his heart without speaking with his tongue, his prayer does not invalidate, as in al-Bahr. He said: (He does bad etiquette) because it is preoccupation from prayer; apparently the dislike is tanzihi, and this is only if intentional; if his sight falls upon it unintentionally and he understands, it is not disliked. He said: (Or eats what is between his teeth) he qualified it because if he takes something from outside, even a sesame seed or a raindrop reaching his throat, his prayer and fast invalidate if he is mindful. He said: (And it is less than a chickpea) but if it is the size of a chickpea or more, it invalidates as it invalidates the fast; what invalidates one invalidates the other, and what does not, does not. He said: (Without much action) but if his chewing is much, there is no disagreement on invalidation as in al-Bahr, unlike swallowing a little with little action because it is a follow-up of his saliva and cannot be avoided. He said: (It is disliked) i.e., in the mosque; and what legal reasoning requires is not to touch it until he finishes his prayer, then throw it in a permissible place and not eat it, for it has been narrated: 'Eat the crumbs and throw away the particles.' Ibn al-Athir said in his Nihaya: Al-wagham is what falls from food, and al-fugham is what the toothpick extracts from between the teeth; i.e., throw away what the toothpick extracts, and likewise what comes out by itself, especially if it stays long enough to change; and if he eats it, it is disliked even outside prayer. He said: (Or suck) he expressed it in this construction for its correctness because it occurs in the most eloquent speech, Allah said: 'Sa'ala sa'ilun.' He said: (Whether woman and dog) he indicated thereby opposition to the Zahiris, who said that her passage in front of him, and likewise dog and donkey, invalidates. He said: (Due to his saying, peace be upon him, etc.) And when Abu Dawud reported from al-Fadl ibn al-Abbas that the Messenger of Allah came to us while we were in our desert and with him was al-Abbas, and he prayed in an open plain with no screen in front of him, and a female dog and donkey were playing in front of him, so what is it to me? He said: (For it is a devil) whether human or otherwise, because the devil generalizes; Allah said: 'Shayatin of humans and jinn' [al-An'am 6:112].
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter 'What Does Not Invalidate Prayer' from Maraqi al-Falah. The matn lists several actions that do not break prayer, and the hashya explains each. First, looking at a written text (whether Quran or otherwise) and understanding it does not invalidate prayer because invalidation requires actual speech (nutaq). The commentator stresses that this is only if the looking is intentional; if unintentional, it is not even disliked. Lack of khushu' is a deficiency in perfection, not validity. Second, eating food particles left between the teeth that are less than a chickpea in size and not requiring much action is disliked but does not invalidate. The reason is the difficulty of avoidance. However, swallowing something from outside the mouth (like a sesame seed or raindrop) invalidates prayer and fast if done knowingly. If the particle is a chickpea-size or more, it invalidates. Much chewing invalidates by consensus. The preferred legal view is to spit out such particles after prayer rather than eat them. Third, sucking (mazz) something is not explicitly in the matn but the commentator clarifies it can be validly expressed. Fourth, the passage of a woman, dog, or donkey in front of the worshipper's prostration place does not invalidate prayer. The hadith 'Nothing cuts the prayer' and the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) are cited as proofs. The Zahiri school's contrary view is noted. The passage concludes that the passing being a devil does not affect validity.

Key Terms
الشيطان (al-shaytan): Devil; here applied to the passing being (woman, dog, donkey) as a metaphorical description, not literal.
الخشوع (al-khushu'): Humility and attentiveness in prayer; its lack does not invalidate but reduces reward.
الحمصة (al-himmisa): A chickpea; used as a measure for the size of food particles that if swallowed may affect validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect on a person's prayer if a dog passes in front of him during salah?
A) The prayer becomes invalid.
B) The prayer remains valid but the dog is considered a devil.
C) The prayer remains valid and the dog's passing is irrelevant.
D) The prayer becomes invalid only if the dog is female.

Key Takeaway
The passing of a woman, dog, or donkey does not invalidate prayer; the only sin is on the deliberate passerby.

Rulings on Actions That Do Not Invalidate Prayer
Explanation of rulings that do not break prayer with commentary on passerby

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which common actions during prayer do not invalidate it and explain the proof from the hadith 'Nothing cuts off prayer'.

Core Idea
Prayer is not invalidated by looking, eating small amounts, or a passerby—only uttering speech or excessive actions break it.

This lesson covers several actions a person might encounter during prayer: looking at written text, eating small food remnants, the presence of a sweet taste, and someone passing in front. While some may be disliked or sinful, they do not nullify the prayer itself. Understanding what does and does not invalidate prayer is crucial for maintaining focus without unnecessary repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify each action and its ruling
List the actions: looking at writing, eating less than a chickpea, swallowing sugar from mouth, passing of woman/dog/donkey. For each, state whether the prayer remains valid or invalid, and whether it is disliked.
The prayer remains valid in all but the sugar case if swallowed during prayer.
2
Locate the primary proof
The hadith 'لا يقطع الصلاة شيء' from Abu Juhaym, narrated in Bukhari and Muslim, is the main evidence that nothing external cuts off prayer.
This hadith is a general (amm) proof.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit negation 'لا يقطع' indicates that no action from outside (like passing) can break the validity of the prayer. The prayer remains intact.
The hadith also advises to ward off the passerby, but that does not affect validity.
4
Analyze the sin of the passerby
Another hadith warns that if the passerby knew the sin, he would stop for forty years. This shows extreme sinfulness but does not affect the prayer's validity.
The text details four scenarios of sin allocation between worshipper and passerby.
5
Note the details on disliked passing
Passing is only disliked in the place of prostration; the definition varies by mosque size, and exception is made in streets due to hardship.
The most correct view (asahh) is that it is disliked in the place of prostration, not the entire row.

Chapter of Prayer - Section on What Does Not Invalidate Prayer: (If the praying person looks at a written text and understands it, whether it is Quran or other, intending to understand or not, he has done ill manners, but his prayer is not invalidated due to not uttering speech. Or if he eats what is between his teeth and it is less than a chickpea without much action, it is disliked and does not invalidate due to difficulty of avoiding it. If he swallows what melted from sugar in his mouth, it becomes invalid. If he swallowed it before prayer and finds its sweetness during prayer, it does not invalidate. Or if a passerby enters in his place of prostration, it does not invalidate) whether woman, dog, or donkey, due to his statement ﷺ: 'Nothing cuts off prayer' and 'ward off as much as you can, for it is only a devil.' And the responsible passerby who deliberately commits a sin due to his statement ﷺ: 'If the passerby knew what is upon him, he would stop for forty - it is better for him than to pass in front of him' narrated by al-Shaykhan, and in the narration of al-Bazzar 'forty autumns'. And passing in the place of prostration is disliked according to the most correct view in the large mosque and desert, and in the small mosque absolutely, and within less than a cubit on which he prays, except beyond that in a street due to causing hardship on the passersby. And his prayer is not invalidated by his looking at the private part of a divorced woman or a non-mahram, meaning her internal private part with desire in the chosen view, because it is a small action, even if it establishes the return (of divorce).

His statement: (the responsible person deliberately) excludes the non-responsible and the non-deliberate, so there is no sin on them. Know that the issue has four aspects as transmitted by al-Shilbi from al-Bada'i' and Ibn Amir Hajj from Ibn Daqiq al-Id: one is that the passerby has an alternative for passing, and the praying person does not involve himself, so the passerby is the sole sinner. The second is its opposite, that the praying person involves himself and the passerby has no alternative, so the praying person alone is sinful. The third is that the praying person involves himself and the passerby has an alternative, so both sin. The fourth is that the praying person does not involve himself and the passerby has no alternative, so neither sins. His statement 'between the hands of the praying person' means near him, and he expressed it with hands (yadayn) because most activity occurs with them, as said by Badr al-‘Ayni in his commentary on al-Bukhari. His statement: (what is upon him) - al-Nawawi said in a narration we transmitted in the Arba'In of ‘Abd al-Qahir al-Rahawi: what sin is upon him. His statement: (he would stop forty - it is better for him) - that which is in al-Jami' al-Saghir from the narration of Malik and the two shaykhs and the four from Abu Jahm: 'he would stop' with the addition of 'an' which is the correct version. Al-Munawi said regarding his statement 'better for him': nasb of 'khayran' as the predicate of 'kana', and raf‘ as its subject and 'yaqif' as the predicate. His statement: (forty autumns) means forty years - naming the whole by its medium part in goodness over its other parts. His statement: (according to the most correct) - Fakhr al-Islam said: it is the place on which a humble gaze falls. Al-Timurtashi said: it is the most correct due to its generality, for he did not choose anything except what is consistent in all cases; he is the Imam who has won the race in the field of verification as in al-‘Inayah, and it was also corrected in al-Nihayah. The investigator in al-Fath said: what appears is the preference of what Fakhr al-Islam chose, and its being without differentiation between mosque and other, for the one who sins is the one who passes between the hands of the praying person in reality, and considering the mosque or house as one place in some rulings does not necessitate changing the sensory matter, and passing from a distance makes the distant close. End. His statement: (in the large mosque) is that it is forty or more, and it is said sixty or more, and the small is its opposite as stated by al-Qahistani, and he stated that the chosen is the first, and the house and home should be on this detail as in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Qahistani. His statement: (and in the small mosque absolutely, unless there is a barrier like a pillar he prays to. His statement: (and within less than a cubit on which he prays) is conjoined to his statement 'place of prostration'. His statement: (except beyond that) which is the measure of a cubit or more, or the passing is in other than the place of prostration in the large mosque and desert. His statement: (because of hardship on passersby) is the reason for his statement 'except beyond that'. His statement: (meaning her internal private part) explicit on what is presumed. His statement: (with desire) - the definition of desire is that the organ becomes erect or its erection increases if it was already erect before, and in the woman,
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (hashiya) on Maraqi al-Falah, explaining several rulings about actions that do not invalidate prayer. The author first discusses looking at written text: if a person in prayer looks at something written and understands it, even if intending to understand, the prayer remains valid because no speech was uttered, but it is disliked (makruh) due to bad manners. Similarly, eating a small amount (less than a chickpea) of food stuck between teeth without significant movement is disliked but not invalidating. However, swallowing something that melted in the mouth, like sugar, does break the prayer. If a sweet taste from something swallowed before prayer remains, it does not invalidate. The second major topic is the passerby (mar). The prayer is not invalidated by someone passing in front, regardless of whether the passer is a woman, dog, or donkey, based on the hadith 'Nothing cuts off prayer.' The hadith about the sin of deliberately passing is also cited, and the commentary details four scenarios of shared responsibility between the worshipper and passerby. The disliked area for passing is defined as the place of prostration (mawdi' al-sujud) in large mosques and open spaces; in small mosques, the entire area is disliked. Beyond a cubit or in streets, it is not disliked due to necessity. Finally, looking at the private part of a divorced or non-mahram woman with desire does not invalidate prayer because it is a small action, though it is sinful. The commentary emphasizes that these actions, while disliked or sinful, do not nullify the validity of the prayer itself.

Key Terms
مار (mār): A person who passes in front of a praying person.
محل السجود (maḥall al-sujūd): The area on the ground where the praying person prostrates; the place of prostration.
مكروه (makrūh): Disliked; an action that is not sinful but contrary to the preferred practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a woman passing in front of a praying person according to the Hanafi school?
A) It invalidates the prayer.
B) It is disliked but does not invalidate.
C) It is permissible without any dislike.
D) It is forbidden and must be stopped.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school firmly holds that prayer is not invalidated by external actions such as looking, eating small amounts, or a passerby; only uttering speech or excessive movement breaks it.

Ruling on Passing in Front of a Praying Person
Explains the ruling and scenarios of passing before one praying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on passing in front of a praying person, identify the four scenarios of sin distribution, and explain the Hanafi preferred opinion regarding the area of prohibition.

Core Idea
Passing before a praying person is makruh tahrimi; sin depends on intent and alternatives.

In this lesson, we examine a well-known hadith warning against passing in front of a praying person, and how Hanafi scholars derive the ruling of makruh tahrimi. The passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi expands on the matn by detailing four scenarios that allocate sin between the passer and the praying person, and clarifies the precise area that triggers the prohibition. Understanding these distinctions prevents common misunderstandings and provides a precise legal framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary evidence
Locate the hadith cited (from Bukhari and Muslim) and note its phrasing: 'If he knew what sin is upon him, standing forty years would be better for him than passing...' This is the core dalil.
The hadith is ahad, which affects the hukm level.
2
Determine the hukm level
Apply Hanafi usul: because the hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), the prohibition does not reach the level of haram but becomes makruh tahrimi. Understand why it is not haram.
The strong wording indicates a severe sin, but not unbelief.
3
Apply the four scenarios
Read the four situations of sin distribution based on the passer's alternative (mandooha) and the praying person's causing. Map each scenario to a real example.
Focus on the allocation of sin: only passer, only praying person, both, or neither.
4
Evaluate the ikhtilaf on the prohibited area
Compare the two opinions: the place of prostration (mahall al-sujud) vs. the range of the humble gaze. Use the arguments from the text to understand why the former is preferred.
Fakhr al-Islam's view is the mufta bihi according to the text.
5
Note practical application
Consider how the ruling differs in large mosque, small mosque, open space, and street, and the exception for narrowing upon passers-by.
The size of the mosque affects whether the prohibition extends beyond the place of prostration.

The one passing in front of the praying person: what sin is upon him? If he knew, standing forty years would be better for him than passing in front of him. Narrated by al-Shaykhayn, and in a narration of al-Bazzar: forty autumns. And it is disliked to pass at the place of prostration on the most correct opinion in the large mosque and the open space, and in the small mosque absolutely, and with a distance less than a man's height he prays upon it, except beyond that in a street due to narrowing upon passers-by. His saying: (the obligatee with intent) excludes the non-obligatee and the non-intentional, so there is no sin upon them. And know that the issue has four aspects as narrated by al-Shalabi from al-Bada'i' and Ibn Amir Hajj from Ibn Daqiq al-'Id: one: the passer has an alternative to passing, and the praying person does not cause it, then the sin is specifically upon the passer. Second, its opposite: the praying person causes the passing, and the passer has no alternative, then the sin is specifically upon the praying person. Third, the praying person causes it, and the passer has an alternative, then both sin. Fourth, the praying person does not cause it, and the passer has no alternative, then neither sins. His saying: 'between the hands of the praying person' means near him...
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi discusses the ruling on a person passing in front of someone who is praying. The matn states that it is severely disliked (makruh) and that it would be better for the passer to stand forty years than to pass, citing the hadith. The commentator then elaborates on four scenarios of sin distribution between the passer and the praying person, clarifying that sin depends on intent and availability of alternative paths. He also defines 'between the hands' as near the praying person and discusses the correct opinion on the area of prostration being the focus, with details on mosque size and distance. The commentary provides a nuanced understanding of responsibility in this act.

Key Terms
المار (al-marr): The person passing in front of the praying person in this context.
المندوحة (al-mandūḥah): An alternative path or way to avoid passing in front of the praying person.
محل السجود (maḥall al-sujūd): The spot on the ground where the praying person prostrates; the area within which passing is disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the passer has no alternative and the praying person does not cause the passing.
B) When the praying person causes the passing and the passer has an alternative.
C) When the passer has an alternative and the praying person does not cause the passing.
D) When neither has an alternative nor causes the passing.

Key Takeaway
Passing in front of a praying person is makruh tahrimi; the sin distribution depends on the presence of alternatives and who caused the situation.

Nullification of Prayer by Looking or Touching Private Parts
Explains when looking or touching a private part nullifies prayer, with Qiyas to intercourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when looking at or touching a private part nullifies prayer, and distinguish between the cases for men and women.

Core Idea
Looking alone does not nullify prayer; touching/kissing with desire does, because it is analogous to intercourse.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced ruling from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi that distinguishes between the effects of looking and touching private parts during prayer. The key principle is that only actions considered 'major' (amal kathir) nullify prayer, and the text uses qiyas to intercourse to classify touching as major. You will learn the precise conditions and the difference between men and women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mental act and its ruling
The matn states that looking at the private part of a divorced or foreign woman does not nullify prayer, even with desire. This is because it is a 'small action' (amal qalil). Note that the chosen view (al-mukhtar) includes looking with desire as non-nullifying.
The text specifies 'inner private part' (al-farj al-dakhil) and 'with desire' to clarify the scope.
2
Distinguish between looking and touching
Touching or kissing, unlike looking, can nullify prayer. However, for a man, it must be done with desire to be in the 'meaning of intercourse' (ma'na al-jima'). For a woman, any kissing or touching by her nullifies her prayer, regardless of her desire, because her act is presumed to involve desire or is analogous to intercourse from the husband's perspective.
The asymmetry is due to the nature of desire: women's desire is more easily aroused.
3
Apply the Qiyas to intercourse
Intercourse (asl) is a major action that nullifies prayer by consensus. The illa (effective cause) is 'being in the meaning of intercourse' – i.e., any act that involves sexual intimacy with desire. Touching/kissing with desire (far') shares this illa, so it also nullifies prayer. The text confirms that the husband's act of kissing/touching, if with desire, is considered like intercourse.
The qiyas is jaliy (explicit) because the illa is clearly stated.
4
Analyze the gender difference
The commentary resolves a potential question: why does a woman's prayer nullify if she kisses a man without his desire, but a man's prayer does not nullify if he kisses a woman without his desire? The answer: the woman's kissing inherently implies her desire (since women's desire is more powerful), and her act is considered in the meaning of intercourse from the husband's side. For the man, without desire, his act is not analogous to intercourse.
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school.

Source Text

قوله: (يعني فرجها الداخل) نص على المتوهم. قوله : (بشهوة) حد الشهوة أن تنتشر الإلة أو يزداد انتشارها إن كانت منتشرة قبل، وفي المرأة، قيلها، أو لمسها فسدت صلاته لأنه في معنى الجماع والجماع عمل كثير ولو كانت تصلى فأولج بين فخذيها، وإن لم ينزل أو قبلها، ولو بدون شهوة أو لمسها بشهوة فسدت صلاتها، وإن قبلته ولم يشتهها لم تفسد صلاته . قوله: (وإن ثبت به الرجعة) أي في المطلقة رجعياً، وتثبت به حرمة المصاهرة في الأجنبية. قوله: (والجماع عمل كثير) أي فكذا ما كان بمعناه فيفسد واعلم أن هذا يفيد تقييد اللمس بالشهوة لأنه لا يكون في معنى الجماع إلا هما وقوله أو لمسها بشهوة أي منه لأنه في معنى الجماع قوله : (لم تفسد صلاته فإن قلت : ما الفرق بين تقبيلها إياه، أو لمسها، وهو يصلي بغير شهوة منه، وبين تقبيله إياها، أو لمسه وهي تصلي بغير شهوة أيضاً حيث تفسد صلاتها لا صلاته. قلت: الفرق أن الشهوة فيهن أبلغ فتقبيله مستلزم لاشتهائها، وأيضاً تقبيله مطلقاً، ومسه بشهوة في معنى الجماع يعني والجماع فعل الزوج ففعله الدواعي كفعله حقيقة الجماع ولو جامعها، ولو بين . تفسد صلاتها، فكذا هذا بخلاف المرأة فإن الجماع ليس فعلها فلا يكون إتيانها بالدواعي في معنى الجماع ما لم يشته الزوج، أفاده الحلبي والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
And his prayer is not nullified by his looking at the private part of a divorced woman or a foreign woman, meaning her inner private part with desire in the chosen view, because it is a small action (and even if it establishes revocability) even if... His saying: (meaning her inner private part) is a text for the suspected. His saying: (with desire) the definition of desire is that the male organ becomes erect or increases in erection if it was already erect, and in a woman, if he kissed her or touched her, his prayer is invalid because it is in the meaning of intercourse, and intercourse is a big action. If a woman is praying and she inserts between her thighs, even if she does not ejaculate, or she kisses him, even without desire, or he touches her with desire, her prayer becomes invalid. If she kisses him and he does not desire it, his prayer does not become invalid. His saying: (and even if it establishes revocability) meaning in a revocable divorced woman, and it establishes the prohibition of marriage connection in a foreign woman. His saying: (and intercourse is a big action) meaning thus anything in its meaning invalidates. And know that this restricts touching to with desire because nothing is in the meaning of intercourse except these two. And his saying: or he touches her with desire means from his side because it is in the meaning of intercourse. His saying: (her prayer does not become invalid). If you say: what is the difference between her kissing him or touching him while he is praying without desire, and his kissing her or touching her while she is praying without desire also, where her prayer becomes invalid but not his? I say: the difference is that desire in women is more powerful, so his kissing entails her desire. Also, his kissing absolutely and his touching with desire is in the meaning of intercourse, meaning intercourse is the act of the husband, so his doing the causes is like his doing the actual intercourse. If he had intercourse with her or [close to it] her prayer becomes invalid, so too this. Unlike the woman, because intercourse is not her act, so her doing the causes is not in the meaning of intercourse unless her husband desires. This is reported from al-Halabi, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi discusses the ruling on nullification of prayer by looking at or touching private parts of a divorced or foreign woman. The matn states that looking alone does not nullify prayer, even if done with desire, because it is considered a minor action. However, touching or kissing with desire nullifies the prayer for a man because it is akin to intercourse, which is a major invalidator. The commentator further distinguishes between men and women: if a woman touches or kisses a man without his desire, her prayer is nullified because women's desire is more easily aroused, and his kissing or touching (even without his desire) implies her desire. But if a man kisses or touches a woman without desire, his prayer remains valid. This asymmetry is based on the difference in how desire operates in men and women, and the fact that intercourse is an act of the husband, not the wife. The text also notes that the ruling applies whether the woman is revocably divorced or foreign, and that such acts establish the prohibition of marriage ties.

Key Terms
الشهوة (al-shahwah): Sexual desire defined as erection for men and arousal for women.
عمل كثير (amal kathir): A major action that nullifies prayer, such as intercourse or acts in its meaning.
معنى الجماع (ma'na al-jima'): Acts that are analogous to sexual intercourse in terms of being major invalidators of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man kisses his wife during prayer without desire, what is the status of his prayer?
A) His prayer is invalid.
B) His prayer is valid.
C) His prayer is makruh but valid.
D) His prayer is invalid only if she felt desire.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, looking alone does not nullify prayer; only touching/kissing with desire (for men) or any touching/kissing by a woman nullifies, based on qiyas to intercourse.
